{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Microsoft and partners aim to shrink the ‘data desert’ limiting accessible AI","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2058806","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">AI-based tools like computer vision and voice interfaces have the potential to be life-changing for people with disabilities, but the truth is those AI models are usually built with very little data sourced <em>from</em> those people. <a href=\"https://blogs.microsoft.com/ai/?p=82372\">Microsoft is working with several nonprofit partners</a> to help make these tools reflect the needs and everyday realities of people living with conditions like blindness and limited mobility.</p>\n<p>Consider for example a computer vision system that recognizes objects and can describe what is, for example, on a table. Chances are that algorithm was trained with data collected by able people, from their point of view — likely standing.</p>\n<p>A person in a wheelchair looking to do the same thing might find the system isn&#8217;t nearly as effective from that lower angle. Similarly a blind person will not know to hold the camera in the right position for long enough for the algorithm to do its work, so they must do so by trial and error.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Or consider a face recognition algorithm that&#8217;s meant to tell when you&#8217;re paying attention to the screen for some metric or another. What&#8217;s the likelihood that among the faces used to train that system, any significant amount have things like a ventilator, or a puff-and-blow controller, or a headstrap obscuring part of it? These &#8220;confounders&#8221; can significantly affect accuracy if the system has never seen anything like them.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"KhQGFVS9RX\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/05/apples-global-accessibility-head-on-the-companys-new-accessibility-features/\">Apple’s global accessibility head on the company&#8217;s new features for iOS 13 and macOS Catalina</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple’s global accessibility head on the company&#8217;s new features for iOS 13 and macOS Catalina&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/05/apples-global-accessibility-head-on-the-companys-new-accessibility-features/embed/#?secret=KhQGFVS9RX\" data-secret=\"KhQGFVS9RX\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Facial recognition software that fails on people with dark skin, or has lower accuracy on women, is a common example of this sort of &#8220;garbage in, garbage out.&#8221; Less commonly discussed but no less important is the visual representation of people with disabilities, or of their point of view.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/microsoft\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"microsoft\">Microsoft <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> today announced a handful of efforts co-led by advocacy organizations that hope to do something about this &#8220;data desert&#8221; limiting the inclusivity of AI.</p>\n<p><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/XewCmUrqIM8?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<p>The first is a collaboration with Team Gleason, an organization formed to improve awareness around the neuromotor degenerative disease amyotrophic lateral sclerosis, or ALS (it&#8217;s named after former NFL star Steve Gleason, who was diagnosed with the disease some years back).</p>\n<p>Their concern is the one above regarding facial recognition. People living with ALS have a huge variety of symptoms and assistive technologies, and those can interfere with algorithms that have never seen them before. That becomes an issue if, for example, a company wanted to ship gaze tracking software that relied on face recognition, as Microsoft would surely like to do.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Computer vision and machine learning don&#8217;t represent the use cases and looks of people with ALS and other conditions,&#8221; said Team Gleason&#8217;s Blair Casey. &#8220;Everybody&#8217;s situation is different and the way they use technology is different. People find the most creative ways to be efficient and comfortable.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"uCFiTKH8q2\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/27/as-ada-turns-30-tech-is-just-getting-started-helping-people-with-disabilities/\">As ADA turns 30, tech is just getting started helping people with disabilities</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;As ADA turns 30, tech is just getting started helping people with disabilities&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/27/as-ada-turns-30-tech-is-just-getting-started-helping-people-with-disabilities/embed/#?secret=uCFiTKH8q2\" data-secret=\"uCFiTKH8q2\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Project Insight is the name of a new joint effort with Microsoft that will collect face imagery of volunteer users with ALS as they go about their business. In time that face data will be integrated with Microsoft&#8217;s existing cognitive services, but also released freely so others can improve their own algorithms with it.</p>\n<p>They aim to have a release in late 2021. If the timeframe seems a little long, Microsoft&#8217;s Mary Bellard, from the company&#8217;s AI for Accessibility effort, pointed out that they&#8217;re basically starting from scratch and getting it right is important.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Research leads to insights, insights lead to models that engineers bring into products. But we have to have data to make it accurate enough to be in a product in the first place,&#8221; she said. &#8220;The data will be shared — for sure this is not about making any one product better, it&#8217;s about accelerating research around these complex opportunities. And that&#8217;s work we don&#8217;t want to do alone.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Another opportunity for improvement is in sourcing images from users who don&#8217;t use an app the same way as most. Like the person with impaired vision or in a wheelchair mentioned above, there&#8217;s a want of data from their perspective. There are two efforts aiming to address this.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2058913\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ORBIT-Hero-Image.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2058913\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2058913\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ORBIT-Hero-Image.png\" alt=\"Images taken by people needing objects in them to be identified or located.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"577\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ORBIT-Hero-Image.png 1460w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ORBIT-Hero-Image.png?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ORBIT-Hero-Image.png?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ORBIT-Hero-Image.png?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ORBIT-Hero-Image.png?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ORBIT-Hero-Image.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2058913\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> ORBIT</p></div></p>\n<p>One with City University of London is the expansion and eventual public release of the Object Recognition for Blind Image Training project, which is assembling a dataset for everyday for identifying everyday objects — a can of pop, a keyring — using a smartphone camera. Unlike other datasets, though, this will be sourced entirely from blind users, meaning the algorithm will learn from the start to work with the kind of data it will be given later anyway.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2058910\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/image-captioning-1-1024x271-1.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2058910\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2058910\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/image-captioning-1-1024x271-1.png\" alt=\"AI captioned images\" width=\"1024\" height=\"271\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/image-captioning-1-1024x271-1.png 1024w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/image-captioning-1-1024x271-1.png?resize=150,40 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/image-captioning-1-1024x271-1.png?resize=300,79 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/image-captioning-1-1024x271-1.png?resize=768,203 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/image-captioning-1-1024x271-1.png?resize=680,180 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/image-captioning-1-1024x271-1.png?resize=50,13 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2058910\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Microsoft</p></div></p>\n<p>The other is an expansion of <a href=\"https://vizwiz.org/tasks-and-datasets/image-captioning/\">VizWiz</a> to better encompass this kind of data. The tool is used by people who need help right away in telling, say, whether a cup of yogurt is expired or if there&#8217;s a car in the driveway. Microsoft worked with the app&#8217;s creator, Danna Gurari, to improve the app&#8217;s existing database of tens of thousands of images with associated questions and captions. They&#8217;re also working to alert a user when their image is too dark or blurry to analyze or submit.</p>\n<p>Inclusivity is complex because it&#8217;s about people and systems that, perhaps without even realizing it, define &#8220;normal&#8221; and then don&#8217;t work outside of those norms. If AI is going to be inclusive, &#8220;normal&#8221; needs to be redefined and that&#8217;s going to take a lot of hard work. Until recently, people weren&#8217;t even talking about it. But that&#8217;s changing.</p>\n<p>&#8220;This is stuff the ALS community wanted years ago,&#8221; said Casey. &#8220;This is technology that exists — it&#8217;s sitting on a shelf. Let&#8217;s put it to use. When we talk about it, people will do more, and that&#8217;s something the community needs as a whole.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Twilio confirms it is buying Segment for $3.2B in an all-stock deal","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059118","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/twilio\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"twilio\">Twilio <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> today <a href=\"https://investors.twilio.com/news/news-details/2020/Twilio-to-Acquire-Segment-the-Market-leading-Customer-Data-Platform/default.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">announced</a> its biggest acquisition to date, spearheading a stronger move into customer data management alongside its existing API-based tools for building and running communications services.</p>\n<p>Twilio is paying $3.2 billion to acquire <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/segment-io\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"segment-io\">Segment, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> a technology startup that lets organizations pull customer data from one app into another, by way of APIs, and use its platform to better control the movement of that customer data, used for marketing and other applications that benefit from customer identification and segmentation.</p>\n<p>This is an all-stock deal &#8212; specifically &#8220;in Twilio Class A common stock, on a fully diluted and cash free, debt free basis&#8221; and it is expected to close in Q4 2020. Segment will become a division of Twilio, the companies said.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The deal was first <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/alexkonrad/2020/10/09/twilio-to-acquire-cloud-startup-segment-for-3-billion/#361825102020\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">reported</a> to be in the works on Friday. (FWIW we&#8217;d also gotten the same tip and had been investigating it when that story got published. Our <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/11/twilio-is-buying-customer-data-startup-segment-for-between-3b-and-4b/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">sources had said</a> the deal was going to be between $3 billion and $4 billion, and announced possibly as soon as today.)</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"M0YFzJU6F8\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/06/twilio-ceo-jeff-lawson-on-shifting-a-3000-person-company-to-fully-remote/\">Twilio CEO Jeff Lawson on shifting a 3,000-person company to fully remote</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Twilio CEO Jeff Lawson on shifting a 3,000-person company to fully remote&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/06/twilio-ceo-jeff-lawson-on-shifting-a-3000-person-company-to-fully-remote/embed/#?secret=M0YFzJU6F8\" data-secret=\"M0YFzJU6F8\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The deal underscores how Twilio is moving deeper into customer engagement services, both for marketing data and other purposes (putting it into closer competition with the likes of Adobe).</p>\n<p>“Data silos destroy great customer experiences,” said Jeff Lawson, co-founder and CEO of Twilio, in a statement. “Segment lets developers and companies break down those silos and build a complete picture of their customer. Combined with Twilio&#8217;s Customer Engagement Platform, we can create more personalized, timely and impactful engagement across customer service, marketing, analytics, product and sales. We are thrilled to welcome Segment to the Twilio team.”</p>\n<p>“Together, Twilio and Segment have an incredible opportunity to build the customer engagement platform of the future,” added Peter Reinhardt, Segment’s co-founder and CEO. “We created Segment to help businesses set themselves apart in the digital age and deliver rich, connected customer experiences built on high-quality data. By joining forces and applying our customer data platform to Twilio’s engagement cloud, we’ll be able to make the entire customer experience seamless from end-to-end.”</p>\n<p>This is Twilio&#8217;s biggest acquisition since it <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/15/twilio-acquires-email-api-platform-sendgrid-for-2-billion-in-stock/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">picked up SendGrid for $2 billion</a> to add email to its range of communications tools back in 2018. Segment was <a href=\"https://news.crunchbase.com/news/segment-raises-175m-for-big-data-infra/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">last valued at $1.5 billion</a> at its last raise.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"BznK76TS9U\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/15/twilio-acquires-email-api-platform-sendgrid-for-2-billion-in-stock/\">Twilio acquires email API platform SendGrid for $2 billion in stock</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Twilio acquires email API platform SendGrid for $2 billion in stock&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/15/twilio-acquires-email-api-platform-sendgrid-for-2-billion-in-stock/embed/#?secret=BznK76TS9U\" data-secret=\"BznK76TS9U\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Acquiring Segment is a natural progression of how Twilio has evolved over the last decade.</p>\n<p>Twilio first made its name as a startup in 2008 by providing an easy way for companies to integrate text and voice services into their apps. Using APIs and a few lines of code, companies could tap into the fast-growing world of smartphone and app usage by putting the tools to communicate with their users directly into their apps.</p>\n<p>Over time, those basic tools have taken more shape with a wider range of communications sources such as email and chatbots, and with a more focused set of applications aimed at different verticals using them, and more tools to enable and better manage customer relations, and also tools to better identify, segment and work with those customers.</p>\n<p>Using acquisitions to build that part of the business is part of the company&#8217;s strategy. One source tells us that Twilio actually tried to acquire <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/intercom/\">Intercom</a>, the customer relations messaging service, back in 2014 and 2015. The companies could not agree on a price at the time, our source said. (Watch this space?)</p>\n<p>These days, Twilio&#8217;s Solutions business is focused on applications in marketing, customer service and customer identity. All of these are big use cases for Segment, which has some 20,000 customers using its platform to &#8220;collect, clean and control&#8221; customer data.</p>\n<p>For Segment, it&#8217;s a big step up in terms of scope and potential companies to target with its tools:</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059168\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2059168\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2059168 size-large\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-1.59.15-PM.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-1.59.15-PM.png 1914w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-1.59.15-PM.png?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-1.59.15-PM.png?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-1.59.15-PM.png?resize=768,433 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-1.59.15-PM.png?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-1.59.15-PM.png?resize=1536,865 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-1.59.15-PM.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2059168\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Source: Twilio</p></div></p>\n<p>Acquiring Segment could also bring more customers to the Twilio platform, opening the door to upselling those customers with other services Twilio offers. And given Segment&#8217;s stated focus on providing better tools to handle customer data more responsibly, in an environment where awareness (and breaches of this area is only growing by the day, it gives Twilio a much stronger product set to speak to that need.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"7R61dg4fpy\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/12/equity-monday-twilio-buys-segment-and-airkit-raises-28m-for-its-low-code-platform/\">Equity Monday: Twilio buys Segment, and Airkit raises  $28M for its low-code platform</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Equity Monday: Twilio buys Segment, and Airkit raises  $28M for its low-code platform&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/12/equity-monday-twilio-buys-segment-and-airkit-raises-28m-for-its-low-code-platform/embed/#?secret=7R61dg4fpy\" data-secret=\"7R61dg4fpy\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>There are also some interesting synergies already. Not only are both built around the architecture of using APIs to integrate other services/port data from one place to another, but there&#8217;s an existing integration between the two, which may be getting used a lot already.</p>\n<p>And as one source pointed out to us, there are already a lot of what the source referred to as &#8220;Xwilions&#8221; (ex-Twilio people) working at the smaller company.</p>\n<p>They include CFO Sandy Smith, advisor Sandy O’Gorman and CSO Colleen Coolidge, who has also hired a number of ex-Twilio engineers.</p>\n<p>You might argue that customer service (the main idea of what Twilio has been building) and customer experience (Segment&#8217;s jam) are different things, but the two are connected: one of the big by-products of communications is data, and companies will be looking for better ways of linking up the creation of it, with the repurposing/use of it. In other words, the two complement each other.</p>\n<p><em>We&#8217;ve updated this post with a few insights from the Twilio/Segment conference call earlier today.</em></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=UB878qYSWyE:yLtO7e0iNP4:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Facebook, in a reversal, will now ban Holocaust denial content under its hate-speech policy","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059209","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/facebook\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"facebook\">Facebook <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> this morning <a href=\"https://about.fb.com/news/2020/10/removing-holocaust-denial-content/\">announced</a> a significant change in how it approaches Holocaust denial content on its social network. For years, the company has been criticized for not taking down this extremely offensive form of content in favor of allowing free speech and <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/explainers/2018/7/20/17590694/mark-zuckerberg-facebook-holocaust-denial-recode\">distancing itself from taking on the responsibilities</a> of a traditional publisher. Today, it&#8217;s reversing that position, saying it will now update its hate-speech policy to &#8220;prohibit any content that denies or distorts the Holocaust.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The company said it made the decision amid a growing number of online hate speech attacks and is a part of Facebook&#8217;s newer efforts to fight the spread of hate speech across its platform.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We have banned more than 250 white supremacist organizations and updated our policies to address militia groups and QAnon,&#8221; explained Facebook in an announcement, authored by Monika Bickert, VP of Content Policy. &#8220;We also routinely ban other individuals and organizations globally, and we took down 22.5 million pieces of hate speech from our platform in the second quarter of this year. Following a year of consultation with external experts, we recently banned anti-Semitic stereotypes about the collective power of Jews that often depicts them running the world or its major institutions,&#8221; the company said.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"gRvQ7aVtrQ\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/facebook-gives-more-details-about-its-efforts-against-hate-speech-before-myanmars-general-election/\">Facebook gives more details about its efforts against hate speech before Myanmar&#8217;s general election</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook gives more details about its efforts against hate speech before Myanmar&#8217;s general election&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/facebook-gives-more-details-about-its-efforts-against-hate-speech-before-myanmars-general-election/embed/#?secret=gRvQ7aVtrQ\" data-secret=\"gRvQ7aVtrQ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Facebook also shared some disturbing statistics representative of how its inaction on this front has impacted the world. It said that according to a recent survey of U.S. adults, ages 18-39, nearly a quarter said they believed the Holocaust was a myth, that it had been exaggerated or that they weren’t sure.</p>\n<p>The company noted, too, that institutions focused on Holocaust research and remembrance, such as Yad Vashem, have stressed that Holocaust education is a key component in combating anti-Semitism.</p>\n<p>As many may recall, Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg once used Holocaust denial as an example of where he thought Facebook shouldn&#8217;t intervene with regard to what&#8217;s posted to its platform. In a 2018 <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/2018/7/18/17575156/mark-zuckerberg-interview-facebook-recode-kara-swisher\">Recode interview</a> and related follow-up, he suggested that Holocaust denial was a wrong idea that he personally found &#8220;deeply offensive,&#8221; but said Facebook shouldn&#8217;t take that content down because &#8220;there are things that different people get wrong.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The issue and its controversy, however, was not a new one to Facebook. Holocaust-denial content has been a longstanding problem for the company &#8212; and one where <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2009/06/15/facebook-employees-speak-their-mind-on-holocaust-denial/\">many employees disagreed</a> with Facebook&#8217;s stated position on the matter. Even <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2009/05/12/facebook-remains-stubbornly-proud-of-position-on-holocaust-denial/\">back in 2009</a>, Facebook had favored the protection of free speech, arguing that it outweighed the negative consequences.</p>\n<p>In the years since, Facebook was found to not only allow Holocaust denial on its platform, but to actively promote it. In <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/aug/16/facebook-algorithm-found-to-actively-promote-holocaust-denial\">a 2020 investigation by U.K.-based counter-extremist organisation Institute for Strategic Dialogue (ISD),</a> Facebook search results would bring up suggestions for denial pages on Facebook. These would also recommend links to publishers who sold revisionist and denial literature, among other things.</p>\n<p>This summer, ADL and other civil rights organizations, like the NAACP and Color of Change, ran a month-long boycott of Facebook advertising in an effort to get Facebook to step up and do something about hate speech on its platform. The effort gained <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/08/01/business/media/facebook-boycott.html\">over 1,000 advertisers</a> and put pressure on the company to make changes.</p>\n<p>Facebook then moved to <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/recode/2020/8/11/21363815/facebook-bans-blackface-anti-semitic-conspiracy-theories\">ban across Facebook and Instagram (for the first time) anti-Semitic conspiracy theories</a> about Jewish people running the world, and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/facebook-qanon-ban/\">began to ban QAnon</a>, which has some anti-Semitic elements. But it stopped short of taking action on Holocaust denial.</p>\n<p>In <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/zuck/posts/10112455086578451\">a public Facebook post</a>, Zuckerberg added:</p>\n<blockquote><p>I&#8217;ve struggled with the tension between standing for free expression and the harm caused by minimizing or denying the horror of the Holocaust. My own thinking has evolved as I&#8217;ve seen data showing an increase in anti-Semitic violence, as have our wider policies on hate speech. Drawing the right lines between what is and isn&#8217;t acceptable speech isn&#8217;t straightforward, but with the current state of the world, I believe this is the right balance.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Facebook says its new decision on this matter does not mean users see an immediate clearing of this sort of content from the platform.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Enforcement of these policies cannot happen overnight. There is a range of content that can violate these policies, and it will take some time to train our reviewers and systems on enforcement,&#8221; Facebook noted.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ltlk6u3U7Z\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/facebook-qanon-ban/\">Facebook says it will ban QAnon across its platforms</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook says it will ban QAnon across its platforms&#8221; 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"India’s Razorpay becomes unicorn after new $100 million funding round","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059049","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Bangalore-headquartered <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/razorpay\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"razorpay\">Razorpay, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> one of the handful of Indian fintech startups that has demonstrated accelerated growth in recent years, has joined the coveted unicorn club after raising $100 million in a new financing round, the payments processing startup said on Monday.</p>\n<p>The new financing round, a Series D, was co-led by Singapore’s sovereign wealth fund <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/gic\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"gic\">GIC <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Sequoia India, the six-year-old Indian startup said. The new round valued the startup at “a little more than $1 billion,” co-founder and chief executive Harshil Mathur told TechCrunch in an interview.</p>\n<p>Existing investors Ribbit Capital, Tiger Global, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/01/15/indias-razorpay-nabs-20m-led-by-yc-tiger-global-for-its-stripe-like-payment-gateway/\">Y Combinator, and Matrix Partners</a> also participated in the round, which brings Razorpay’s total to-date raise to $206.5 million.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><a href=\"http://razorpay.com/\">Razorpay</a> accepts, processes, and disburses money online for small businesses and enterprises. In recent years, the startup has expanded its offerings to provide loans to businesses and also launched <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/11/22/razorpay-credit-card-current-account-neo-bank/\">a neo-banking platform to issue corporate credit cards</a>, among other products.</p>\n<p>Mathur and Shashank Kumar (pictured above), who met each other at IIT Roorkee, started Razorpay in 2014. They began to explore opportunities around payments processing business after realizing just how difficult it was for small businesses such as young startups to accept money online less than a decade ago. There were very few payment processing firms in India then and startups needed to produce a long-list of documents.</p>\n<p>The early team of about 11 people at Razorpay shared a single apartment as the co-founders rushed to meet with over 100 bankers to convince banks to work with them. The conversations were slow and remained in a deadlock for so long that the co-founders felt helpless explaining the same challenge to investors numerous times, they recalled in an interview last year.</p>\n<p>To say things have changed for Razorpay would be an understatement. It’s become the largest payments provider for business in India, said Mathur. Razorpay, which competes with Prosus Ventures&#8217; PayU, accepts a wide-range of payment options including credit cards, debit cards, mobile wallets, and UPI.</p>\n<p>“Razorpay has established itself as a clear leader, with its strong focus on customer experience and product innovation,” said Choo Yong Cheen, Chief Investment Officer for Private Equity at GIC, in a statement. “GIC has a long track record of partnering with leading fintech companies globally and is delighted to partner with Razorpay in its journey to transform payments and banking.”</p>\n<p>Some of Razorpay’s clients include budget lodging decacorn Oyo, fintech firm Cred, social giant Facebook, e-commerce Flipkart top food delivery startups <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/zomato\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"zomato\">Zomato <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Swiggy, online learning platform Byju’s, supply chain platform Zilingo, travel ticketing firms Yatra and Goibibo, and telecom giant <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/bharti-airtel-ltd\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"bharti-airtel-ltd\">Airtel <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>.</p>\n<p>The startup expects to process about $25 billion in transactions &#8212; up five times from last year &#8212; for nearly 10 million of its customers this year, said Mathur.</p>\n<p>He attributed some of the growth to the coronavirus pandemic, which he said has accelerated the digital adoption among many businesses.</p>\n<p>On the neo-banking and capital side, Mathur said, Razorpay expects RazorpayX and Razorpay Capital to account for about 35% of the startup’s revenue by the end of March next year.</p>\n<p>Mathur said the startup’s payment processing service continues to be its fastest growing business and does not need much capital to grow, so the startup will be deploying the fresh funds to expand its neo-banking offerings to include vendor payment, and expense and tax management and other features.</p>\n<p>The startup, which aims to work with over 50 million businesses by 2025, may also acquire a few firms as it explores opportunities around inorganic expansion in the neo-banking category, said Mathur.</p>\n<p>“We will continue to make an impactful contribution to the growth of the industry, aid adoption in the under-served markets and drive new practices and a new thinking for the industry to follow. And this investment fits perfectly with our growth strategy,” he said.</p>\n<p>While the coronavirus pandemic has slowed down deal-makings in India, about half a dozen startups in the country including <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/02/indias-online-learning-platform-unacademy-raises-150-million-at-1-45-billion-valuation/\">online leaning platform Unacademy</a>, and Pine Labs have secured the unicorn status.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=nE5sMKwGyrk:Qx0FZbzr_Uw:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"AC Ventures announces the first close of its $80 million fund for Indonesian startups","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059026","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As one of the world’s most populated countries, with a <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/documents/47/SEA_Internet_Economy_Report_2019.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">fast-growing internet economy</a>, Indonesia offers plenty of opportunity for startups. AC Ventures wants to tap into that with its $80 million ACV Capital III L.P. fund. The firm announced the first close of the fund today, with $56 million already committed.</p>\n<p>The capital will be invested into 30 Indonesian startups over the next three years, with first checks of up to $3 million going to seed to Series A-stage companies.</p>\n<p>Based in Jakarta with a team of twelve people, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/acv-auctions\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"acv-auctions\">ACV <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> is a strategic alliance between <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/acventures\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"acventures\">AC Ventures <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Indies Capital. ACV’s founding partners are Adrian Li and Michael Soerijadji, both founders and managing partners at AC Ventures, and Indies Capital managing partner Pandu Sjahrir. Sjahrir is also on the board of two Indonesian unicorns, Gojek and Sea.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The alliance has already made investments in nine startups: Shipper, Kargo, Stockbit, Bukuwarung, ESB, Co-Learn, KitaBeli, Aruna and Soul Parking. It will focus on e-commerce, financial tech, startups that serve MSMEs (or micro, small and medium-sized enterprises) and digital media-enabled services, which Li told TechCrunch could encompass sectors like education and healthcare, in addition to entertainment.</p>\n<p>ACV also plans to work closely with the companies it invests in, guiding them through business development, key executive hires and later rounds of funding. Its also launched programs like AC Academy to coach founders on skills like growth hacking and fundraising.</p>\n<p>Internet penetration and online payments have grown a lot over the past five years, but e-commerce still accounts for a tiny fraction of <a href=\"https://www.jpmorgan.com/europe/merchant-services/insights/reports/indonesia\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Indonesia’s overall retail market</a>. This gives startups plenty of room to innovate. For example, logistics is very fragmented in Indonesia, because it has 600 inhabited islands. Shipper, another ACV investment, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/09/18/shipper-a-platform-for-e-commerce-logistics-in-indonesia-raises-5-million/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">offers a platform </a>to help sellers manage multiple shipments through different providers at once.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Akwpmfoqo0\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/09/18/shipper-a-platform-for-e-commerce-logistics-in-indonesia-raises-5-million/\">Shipper, a platform for e-commerce logistics in Indonesia, raises $5 million</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Shipper, a platform for e-commerce logistics in Indonesia, raises $5 million&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/09/18/shipper-a-platform-for-e-commerce-logistics-in-indonesia-raises-5-million/embed/#?secret=Akwpmfoqo0\" data-secret=\"Akwpmfoqo0\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Fundraising for ACV Capital III began before the COVID-19 pandemic and despite the crisis’ economic toll, Li said that in countries like Indonesia, it may speed up the adoption of many kinds of technology. For example, BukuWarung, which <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/28/indonesian-fintech-startup-bukuwarung-gets-new-funding-to-add-financial-services-for-small-merchants/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">focuses on digitizing operations for neighborhood shops</a> and other small businesses, recently launched digital payments in response to demand for online orders and contactless payments. Another ACV portfolio company, ESB, is <a href=\"https://www.dealstreetasia.com/stories/ac-ventures-esb-187109/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">doing the same thing for restaurants</a>, and Li said interest in its services increased as food and beverage businesses turned to online orders and deliveries during social distancing measures.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We’re really seeing some great opportunities in Indonesia, and we’re seeing more interest globally going into startups in Indonesia,&#8221; said Li. &#8220;This is the world’s fourth most populous country and there are so many products and services which can be delivered better and more efficiently through technology.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Quince launches out of beta with new ‘manufacturer-to-customer’ model","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059166","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The retail landscape is shifting rapidly. While D2C brands have changed the way we shop, <a href=\"https://www.onequince.com/\">Quince</a> is looking to change retail even more dramatically.</p>\n<p>The brand, which raised $8.5 million in seed funding last year (and only revealed as much today), is looking to rethink the supply chain with its own line of 700 items including men&#8217;s and women&#8217;s apparel, accessories, jewelry and home goods.</p>\n<p>After beta testing for a year as &#8216;Last Brand,&#8217; <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/last-brand\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"last-brand\">Quince <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> is launching with a new model called &#8216;M2C,&#8217; or manufacturer to consumer.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The idea is that Quince goes directly to factories with designs for essentials &#8212; not overly patterned or branded items &#8212; with an order that can dynamically adjust each week based on demand. As orders start coming in, Quince can work alongside manufacturers to ensure they aren&#8217;t over or under producing on a specific SKU. The factory then ships directly to the customer, rather than shipping to a distribution center or store and then again to the final destination.</p>\n<p>You might think that factories wouldn&#8217;t be as amenable to this model, as they have little to lose when a brand overestimates demand for a SKU and doesn&#8217;t sell it through to the customer. But cofounder and CEO Sid Gupta says that this new model is being presented at a pivotal time in retail. Bigger brands, the ones that place orders for 100,000 units, are struggling during the pandemic and shrinking their SKU portfolio.</p>\n<p>This leaves the factories with two options: turning to D2C brands or selling through a marketplace like Amazon.</p>\n<p>&#8220;D2C demand is really fragmented, and most D2C companies are really sub-scale,&#8221; said Gupta. &#8220;It&#8217;s hard to get the efficiency gains out of it. The issue with selling on a marketplace, like Amazon, is you&#8217;ve got to compete with hundreds, if not thousands, of other sellers for the same exact good. If you&#8217;re a factory that actually makes high quality goods, and you pay your workers fairly, and you don&#8217;t damage the environment, your cost might be 3% or 5%, higher.&#8221;</p>\n<p>He added that it&#8217;s difficult for a factory to have those factors shine through to the customer on Amazon, and more difficult still to learn how to play the advertising game.</p>\n<p>This environment has made manufacturers slightly more open to a new way of doing things.</p>\n<p>By working directly with factories, Quince says it&#8217;s able to bring the cost of luxury items down significantly, selling a cashmere sweater for approximately $50 instead of $150+, as you&#8217;ll often find with other brands. Quince works with more than 30 different factories across the world.</p>\n<p>Cofounder and CEO Sid Gupta says the company has also thought very deeply about sustainability, setting standards around the materials used (are they organic or recycled?), the manufacturing process (is it ecologically sound?), worker pay, and more. The company is also looking into giveback programs to share in the profits with the factories and the workers.</p>\n<p>The funding from last fall has allowed Quince to beta test last year and grow the team to 16, including cofounders Becky Mortimer and Sourabh Mahajan. Thirty-five percent of employees are female, and 65 percent of employees are minorities.</p>\n<p>The company&#8217;s investors include Founders Fund, 8VC and Basis Set Ventures.</p>\n<div 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Thailand’s logistics startup Flash Express raises $200 million","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059100","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Flash Express, a two-year-old logistics startup that works with e-commerce firms in Thailand, said on Monday it has raised $200 million in a new financing round as it looks to double down on a rapidly growing market spurred by demand due to the coronavirus pandemic.</p>\n<p>The funding, a Series D, was led by PTT Oil and Retail Business Public Company Limited, the marquee oil and retail businesses of Thai conglomerate PTT. Durbell and Krungsri Finnovate, two other top conglomerates in the Southeast Asian country, also participated in the round, which brings Flash Express’ to-date raise to about $400 million.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://flashexpress.com\">Flash Express</a>, which operates door-to-door pickup and delivery service, claims to be the second largest private player to operate in this space. The startup, which also counts Alibaba as an investor, entered the market with delivery fees as low as 60 cents per parcel, a move that allowed it to quickly win a significant market share.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The startup has also expanded aggressively in the past year. Flash Express had about 1,100 delivery points during this time last year. Now it has over 5,000, exceeding those of 138-year-old Thailand Post.</p>\n<p>Flash Express currently delivers more than 1 million parcels a day, up from about 50,000 during the same time last year. The startup says it has also invested heavily in technology that has enabled it to handle over 100,000 parcels in a minute by fully automated sorting systems.</p>\n<p>Komsan Lee, CEO of Flash Express, said the startup plans to deploy the fresh funds to introduce new services and expand to other Southeast Asian markets (names of which he did not identify). “We are also prepared to create and develop new technologies to achieve even greater delivery and logistics efficiency. More importantly we intend to assist SMEs in lowering their investment costs which we believe will provide long-term benefit for the overall Thai economy in the digital era,” he said.</p>\n<p>Retail Business Public Company Limited plans to leverage Flash Express’ logistics network as it looks to meet the rising demand from consumers, said Rajsuda Rangsiyakull, Senior Executive Vice President for Corporate Strategy, Innovation and Sustainability at Retail Business Public Company Limited.</p>\n<p>Flash Express competes with Best Express &#8212; which, like Flash, is also backed by Alibaba &#8212; and Kerry Express, which <a href=\"https://www.bangkokpost.com/business/1975079/kerry-express-thailand-prepares-ipo-for-up-to-300m-shares\">filed</a> for an initial public offering in late August.</p>\n<p>Even as online shopping and delivery has accelerated in recent months, some estimates <a href=\"https://www.bangkokpost.com/business/1981603/logistics-set-to-see-b200bn-income-loss\">suggest</a> that the overall logistics market in Thailand will see its first contraction in the history this year. Chumpol Saichuer, president of the Thai Transportation and Logistics Association, said last month Thailand&#8217;s logistics business has already been hit hard by the slowing global economy.</p>\n<div id=\"speakable-summary\">As the American election looms and the IPO cycle slows some, it&#8217;s a good time to review how well the public offerings we have seen thus far have performed.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><strong><em>The Exchange explores startups, markets and money. We&#8217;ll be awarding letter grades for post-IPO performance as well, because we can.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/subscribe/?tpcc=theexchange\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignright wp-image-1995211 size-medium\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?w=300\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg 900w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?resize=768,768 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-grn.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></a>So, how did Snowflake do compared to Vroom, both stacked next to JFrog and One Medical? Let&#8217;s find out.</p>\n<h2>Ranking 2020&#8217;s IPOs</h2>\n<p>The fine folks at my former publication Crunchbase News have a <a href=\"https://news.crunchbase.com/news/heres-who-has-gone-public-in-2020-so-far/\">running list of 2020 IPOs</a>, which will help us not miss any names. Of course, we&#8217;re not going to include <em>every</em> possible deal; there have been some marginal debuts that we can leave behind.</p>\n<p>But, the majors matter. So let&#8217;s get into them now:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Snowflake: </strong>It priced <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/14/snowflake-and-jfrog-raise-ipo-ranges-as-tech-markets-stay-hot/\">above its raised range</a>. Then it went up sharply. From an IPO price of $120 per share, Snowflake is worth $250 per share today. That&#8217;s so expensive, compared to the data-focused <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/snowflake-computing\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"snowflake-computing\">Snowflake&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> revenue, that I can hardly figure out what the hell its price means. The company&#8217;s valuation <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/19/was-snowflakes-ipo-mispriced-or-just-misunderstood/\">got so rich</a> that <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/16/go-public-now-while-software-valuations-make-no-sense-part-ii/\">we wrote that all tech companies should go public to take advantage of the rich market</a>. This year&#8217;s standout IPO. <strong>A+</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Unity:</strong> Unity&#8217;s IPO was a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/10/how-unity-built-a-gaming-engine-for-the-future/\">source of wonder</a> for those curious about the economics of the gaming world. For us finance dorks, it was also a right corker. We <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/24/unitys-ipo-numbers-look-pretty-unreal/\">were impressed</a>. So were investors. After setting a $34 and $42 per share IPO range, Unity raised it to $44 and $48 per share. Then it went public at $52 per share. Today it&#8217;s worth $94.50 per share, or around $25 billion. It was priced at $6 billion, give or take, in its final private round. 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"China’s digital yuan tests leap forward in Shenzhen","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059110","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/shenzhen-eb7c\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"shenzhen-eb7c\">Shenzhen, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> known for its maker community and manufacturing resources, is taking the lead in trialing China&#8217;s digital yuan.</p>\n<p>Last week, the city <a href=\"https://mp.weixin.qq.com/s/GKH3feEEN0nfIdG6xk0QJQ\">issued</a> 10 million yuan worth of digital currency to 50,000 randomly selected residents who applied. The government doled out the money through mobile &#8220;red envelopes,&#8221; a tool designed to digitize the custom of gifting money in red packets and first popularized by WeChat&#8217;s e-wallet.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Red packets are a common way we’ve seen in China Internet companies to spur adoption like what we’ve seen with Tencent WeChat and Alibaba’s Alipay in the early days, when these products were first launched,&#8221; Flex Yang, CEO of crypto finance firm <a href=\"https://babel.finance/\">Babel Finance</a>, told TechCrunch.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The digital yuan is not to be mistaken as a form of cryptocurrency. Rather, it is issued and managed by the central bank, serving as the statutory, digital version of China&#8217;s physical currency and giving Beijing a better grasp of its currency circulation. It&#8217;s meant to supplement, not replace, third-party payments apps like WeChat Pay and Alipay in a country where cash is dying out.</p>\n<p>For example, the central government may in the future issue subsidies to local offices by sending digital yuan, which can help tackle issues like corruption.</p>\n<p>Shenzhen is one of the four Chinese cities to begin internal testing of the digital yuan, announced a government <a href=\"http://www.gov.cn/zhengce/zhengceku/2020-08/14/5534759/files/14eea66b12b34591a7facf3b2b9ed57d.pdf\">notice</a> in August without going into the specifics. The latest distribution to consumers is seen as the country&#8217;s first large-scale, public test of the centrally issued virtual currency.</p>\n<p>Nearly 2 million individuals in Shenzhen signed up for the lottery, according to a<a href=\"https://mp.weixin.qq.com/s/zRHPsafva8PWtTaSHBL2Tg\"> post</a> from the local government. Winners could redeem the 200 yuan red envelope within the official digital yuan app and spend the virtual money at over 3,000 retail outlets in the city.</p>\n<p>There were previous indications of an incoming app. In April, Shenzhen&#8217;s digital currency vehicle launched a <a href=\"https://zhuanlan.zhihu.com/p/136963924\">wave of recruiting</a> for technical positions like mobile app architects and Android developers.</p>\n<p>As its next step, Shenzhen will launch a &#8220;fintech innovation platform&#8221; through its official digital currency institute, said a new <a href=\"http://www.gov.cn/zhengce/2020-10/11/content_5550408.htm\">central government document</a> detailing the city&#8217;s five-year development measures, including attracting more foreign investment in cutting-edge technologies. The city will also play a key role in furthering the digital yuan&#8217;s research and development, application and international collaboration.</p>\n<p>The &#8220;fintech innovation platform&#8221; is vaguely defined in the announcement, but Babel&#8217;s Yang offered his interpretation, pointing out that it is &#8220;designed to allow private enterprises and other institutions to participate in these real-world or capital market development projects that aim to collectively grow the adoption of the DCEP [digital currency electronic payment].&#8221;</p>\n<p>The city is well-positioned to test private involvement for it has been a national model for market-driven economic reforms. Established in 1980 as China&#8217;s first special economic zones, it is now home to tech behemoths like Tencent, Huawei and DJI and innovation hubs like HAX and Trouble Maker. President Xi Jinping <a href=\"https://uk.reuters.com/article/us-china-shenzhen/chinas-xi-to-deliver-speech-in-shenzhen-marking-its-40th-anniversary-state-media-idUKKBN26X08M\">is scheduled to visit the city this week</a> to commemorate the city&#8217;s 40th anniversary.</p>\n<p>While the central bank provides the logic and infrastructure undergirding the digital yuan, there&#8217;s much room for commercial banks and private firms to innovate on the application level. Both ride-hailing platform <a href=\"https://www.coindesk.com/chinas-uber-didi-said-to-trial-pbocs-central-bank-digital-currency\">Didi</a> and <a href=\"https://mp.weixin.qq.com/s/0yuJ4OhExsrC1wDdfmu-1g\">JD&#8217;s fintech arm</a> have recently unveiled steps to help accelerate the digital yuan&#8217;s real-life implementation.</p>\n<p>&#8220;If the pilot [in Shenzhen] goes well, we can anticipate other cities will launch their pilot programs, along with new application scenarios, thus accelerating the adoption of the DCEP,&#8221; observed Yang.</p>\n<p><em>The story is updated on October 12 with expert comments.</em></p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"></audio></p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"></audio></p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"></audio></p>\n<p><audio side","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059058","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/nest\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"nest\">Nest <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> unit today launched its <a href=\"https://store.google.com/us/product/nest_thermostat\">newest thermostat</a>. At $129, the Nest Thermostat is the company&#8217;s most affordable one yet, but it&#8217;s also the first to feature a new swipe and tap interface on its side, as well as Google&#8217;s <a href=\"https://atap.google.com/soli/\">Soli radar technology</a> to sense room occupancy and when you are near the device.</p>\n<p>Soli, it is worth noting, is not being used for enabling gesture controls. Instead, because the design team wanted a solid mirror finish on the front, Nest decided to use it purely for motion sensing.</p>\n<p>The new thermostat, which is made from 49% recycled plastic, will come in four colors: Snow, Charcoal, Sand and Fog. The company is also launching a $14.99 trim kit to help you hide any imperfections in your paint when you install the new thermostat.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059059\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2059059\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2059059\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png 3200w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_all-colors.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2059059\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Nest</p></div></p>\n<p>&#8220;It has this inviting form with this intuitive swipe up and down control, which lets you interact with this product really naturally, instead of pressing these tiny little buttons that most traditional thermostats have,&#8221; Nest product lead Ruchi Desai told me.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s worth noting that this new version is mostly meant for users in smaller apartments or condos, as it doesn&#8217;t support Nest&#8217;s <a href=\"https://store.google.com/us/product/nest_temperature_sensor\">remote sensors</a>. To get support for those, you&#8217;ll need a Nest Thermostat E (which can occasionally be found for around $139) or the fully fledged Nest Learning <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/thermostat\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"thermostat\">Thermostat <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"9So1alV03F\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/29/google-nest-begins-testing-hvac-alerts-partners-with-handy-for-booking-service-calls/\">Google Nest begins testing HVAC alerts, partners with Handy for booking service calls</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Google Nest begins testing HVAC alerts, partners with Handy for booking service calls&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/29/google-nest-begins-testing-hvac-alerts-partners-with-handy-for-booking-service-calls/embed/#?secret=9So1alV03F\" data-secret=\"9So1alV03F\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Talking about learning, among the features the team is highlighting with this release is the thermostat&#8217;s ability to help you schedule your custom temperature settings for different times of the day &#8212; and different days. Nest calls this Quick Schedule.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Unlike the Nest Learning Thermostat, which has the auto-schedule [feature], this one actually offers the ability to create temperature presets, which gives you the ability to set up a schedule based on your lifestyle, based on your preferences,&#8221; Desai said. &#8220;It will also give you the flexibility of holding temperatures, which means it&#8217;ll override the schedule that you have in times when you need the control and flexibility.&#8221;</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059203\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2059203\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2059203\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg 14204w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg?resize=150,112 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Charcoal-Side.jpg?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2059203\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Nest</p></div></p>\n<p>That sounds a lot like what you&#8217;d find in most of today&#8217;s smart thermostats from the likes of Ecobee and other Nest competitors, but it&#8217;s a first for Nest.</p>\n<p>With its Savings Finder feature, the thermostat can also look for small optimizations and suggest minor tweaks that can result in additional energy savings.</p>\n<p>Thanks to the new built-in Soli radar chip, the device can automatically lower the temperature when you&#8217;re not home. It&#8217;s a shame the team isn&#8217;t using the chip for any gesture controls, something Google did with its Pixel 4 phone, but the team tells me that it decided not to do this because it didn&#8217;t fit the user profile.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I think that was a very conscious decision we made while designing this product, because for this product we really have the user in mind and we really wanted to focus on the features that were really important to this user. And these are brand new to smart home, they really wanted app control &#8212; it seems so basic to us but it&#8217;s a massive upgrade for them, right. And all these energy-saving features that come with the thermostat were something that they valued a lot. So we wanted to focus on the features that these users valued for this product,&#8221; Desai explained.</p>\n<p>Maybe we&#8217;ll see Nest do more with this technology in the next iterations of its more expensive thermostats. For now, it feels like a bit of a missed opportunity, though in all fairness, Soli in the Pixel 4 mostly felt like a gimmick and at least the Nest team is putting it to practical use here.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059060\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2059060\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2059060\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png 3600w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png?resize=680,454 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png?resize=2048,1366 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Lifestyle-1.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2059060\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Nest</p></div></p>\n<p>Like before, Nest promises that it will only take about half an hour or so to install the new thermostat. The app walks you through the individual steps, which should make the process pretty straightforward, assuming your heating and cooling system follows modern standards.</p>\n<p>To control the thermostat remotely, you&#8217;ll use the Google Home app, where you&#8217;ll also find all of the smart features to help you save more energy.</p>\n<p><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/20367DapHlc?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<p>The new thermostat is now available in the U.S. (for $129.99) and Canada (for $179.99 CAD). In Canada, the trim kit will retail for $19.99 CAD). As the team noted, between various utility rebates and rewards, a lot of users may be able to get theirs for only a few dollars, depending on where they live.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059062\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Nest-Thermostat_Snow-Front.jpg\"><img
