Wilhelm","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn21@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-34-245_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn43@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-47-798_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn73@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-46-413_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=upXSOHI2eMw:GBUzRjVb7TE:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn96@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-04-47-461_262130e7f182d2c1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=upXSOHI2eMw:GBUzRjVb7TE:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn77@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-48-944_b1e462471fa15e58.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn77@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-48-385_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/upXSOHI2eMw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn23@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-47-673_93f5ede5e6cbe695.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522266663},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Hands on with Telepath, the social network taking aim at abuse, fake news and, to some extent, ‘free speech’","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2058122","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">There&#8217;s no doubt that modern social networks have let us down. Filled with hate speech and abuse, moderation and anti-abuse tools were an afterthought they&#8217;re now trying to cram in. Meanwhile, personalization engines deliver us only what will keep us engaged, even if it&#8217;s not the truth. Today, a number of new social networks are trying to flip the old model on its head &#8212; whether that&#8217;s attempting to use audio for more personal connections, like Clubhouse, eliminate clout chasing, like Twelv, or, in the case of new social network <a href=\"https://www.telepath.com/\">Telepath</a>, by designing a platform guided by rules that focus on enforcing kindness, countering abuse, and disabling the spread of fake news.</p>\n<p>Many of these early efforts are already facing challenges.</p>\n<p>Private social network <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/18/clubhouse-app-chat-rooms/\">Clubhouse</a> has repeatedly demonstrated that allowing free-flowing communication in the form of audio conversations is an area that&#8217;s notoriously difficult to moderate. The app, though still unavailable to the broader public, <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-09-29/private-social-app-clubhouse-courts-fresh-controversy?sref=gni836kR\">courted controversy in September</a> when it allowed anti-Semitic content to be discussed in one of its chat rooms. In the past, it had also allowed users to <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/interface/2020/7/8/21316172/clubhouse-content-moderation-taylor-lorenz-harassment-abuse\">harass</a> an NYT reporter openly.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Meanwhile, <a href=\"https://twelv.com/\">Twelv</a>, a sort of Instagram alternative, ditches the &#8220;Like&#8221; button concept and all the other features now overloading Instagram, which had once been just a photo-sharing network. But, unfortunately, this also means there&#8217;s no easy way to find and follow interesting users or trends on Twelv &#8212; you have to push friends to join the app with you or know someone&#8217;s username to look them up, otherwise it shows you no content. The result is a social network without the &#8220;social.&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.telepath.com/\">Telepath</a>, meanwhile, is a more interesting development.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s pursuing an even loftier goal in social networking &#8212; creating a hate speech-free platform where fake news can&#8217;t be distributed.</p>\n<p>No social network to date has been able to accomplish what Telegraph claims it will be able to do in terms of content moderation. Its ambitions are optimistic and, as the network remains in private beta, they&#8217;re also untested at scale.</p>\n<p>Though positioned as a different kind of social network, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/telepath\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"telepath\">Telepath <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> isn&#8217;t actually focused on developing a new sharing format that could encourage participation &#8212; the way TikTok popularized the 15-second video clip, for example, or how Snapchat turned the world onto &#8220;Stories.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Instead, Telepath, at first glance, looks very much like just another feed to scroll through. (And given the amount of linked Twitter content in Telepath posts, it&#8217;s almost serving as a backchannel for the rival platform.)</p>\n<p>The startup itself was founded by former Quora employees, including <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/05/26/marc-bodnick/\">former</a> Quora Business &#38; Community head, <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/marcbodnick/\">Marc Bodnick</a>, now Telepath Executive Chairman; and former Quora Product Lead, <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/richard-henry-a98a881b3/\">Richard Henry</a>, now Telepath CEO. They&#8217;re aided by former Quora Global Writer Relations Lead, Tatiana Estévez, now Telepath Head of Community and Safety; and Ro Applewhaite, previously research staff for Pete Buttigieg for America, now Telepath Head of Outreach.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s backed by a couple million in seed funding, led by First Round Capital (Josh Kopelman). Other backers include Unusual Ventures (Andy Johns), Slow Ventures (Sam Lessin), and unnamed angels. Bodnick and his wife, Michelle Sandberg, also invested.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2058472\" style=\"width: 324px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2058472\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2058472\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot1.png?w=314\" alt=\"\" width=\"314\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot1.png 1242w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot1.png?resize=69,150 69w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot1.png?resize=139,300 139w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot1.png?resize=768,1662 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot1.png?resize=314,680 314w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot1.png?resize=710,1536 710w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot1.png?resize=946,2048 946w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot1.png?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 314px) 100vw, 314px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2058472\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Telepath</p></div></p>\n<p>When talking about Telepath, it&#8217;s clear the founders are nostalgic for the early days of the web &#8212; before all the people joined, that is. In smaller, online communities in years past, people connected and made internet friends who would become real-world friends. That&#8217;s a moment in time they hope to recapture.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I&#8217;ve benefited a lot by meeting people through the internet, forming relationships and having conversations &#8212; that sort of thing,&#8221; says Henry. &#8220;But the internet just isn&#8217;t fun in the ways that it used to be fun.&#8221;</p>\n<p>He suggests that the anonymity offered by networks like Reddit and Twitter make it more difficult for people to make real-world connections. Telepath, with its focus on conversations, aims to change that.</p>\n<p>&#8220;If we facilitate a really fun, kind, and empathetic conversation environment, then lots of good things can happen. And it might be that you potentially find someone you want to work with, or you end up getting a job, or you meet new friends, or you end up meeting offline,&#8221; Henry says.</p>\n<h2><strong>Getting Started</strong></h2>\n<p>To get started on Telepath, you join the network with your mobile phone number and name, find and follow other users, similar to Twitter, then join interest-based communities as you would on Reddit. When you launch the app, you&#8217;re meant to browse a home feed where conversation topics from your communities and interesting replies are highlighted &#8212; orange for those replies from people you follow and gray for those that Telepath has determined are worth being elevated to the home screen.</p>\n<p>As you read through the posts and visit the communities, you can &#8220;Thumbs Up&#8221; content you like, downvote what you don&#8217;t, reply, mute, block, and use @usernames to flag someone.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059003\" style=\"width: 413px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2059003\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\" wp-image-2059003\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Image-from-iOS.jpg?w=598\" alt=\"\" width=\"403\" height=\"312\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Image-from-iOS.jpg 598w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Image-from-iOS.jpg?resize=150,116 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Image-from-iOS.jpg?resize=300,232 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Image-from-iOS.jpg?resize=50,39 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 403px) 100vw, 403px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2059003\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Telepath, screenshot via TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>Another interesting design choice: everything on Telepath disappears after 30 days. No one will get to dig through your misinformed posts from a decade ago to shame you in the present, it seems.</p>\n<p>What&#8217;s most different about Telepath, however, is not the design or format. It&#8217;s what&#8217;s taking place behind the scenes, as detailed by Telepath&#8217;s rules.</p>\n<p>Users who join Telepath must agree to &#8220;be kind,&#8221; which is rule number one. They must also not attack one another based on identity or harass others. They must use a real name (or their preferred name, if transgender), and not post violent content or porn. &#8220;Fake news&#8221; is banned, as determined by a publisher&#8217;s attempts at disseminating misinformation on a regular basis.</p>\n<p>Telepath has even tried to formalize rules around how polite conversations should function online with rules like &#8220;don&#8217;t circle the drain&#8221; &#8212; meaning don&#8217;t keep trying to have the last word in a contentious debate or circumvent a locked thread; and &#8220;stay on topic,&#8221; which means don&#8217;t bombard a pro-x network with an anti-x agenda (and vice versa.)</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2058469\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2058469\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2058469\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathRules.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"429\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathRules.png 4875w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathRules.png?resize=150,95 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathRules.png?resize=300,189 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathRules.png?resize=768,484 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathRules.png?resize=680,429 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathRules.png?resize=1536,968 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathRules.png?resize=2048,1291 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathRules.png?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2058469\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Telepath</p></div></p>\n<p>To enforce its rules, Telepath begins by requiring users to sign up with a mobile phone number, which is verified as a &#8220;real&#8221; number associated with a SIM card, and not a virtual one &#8212; like the kind you could grab through a &#8220;burner&#8221; app.</p>\n<p>In order to the create its &#8220;kind environment,&#8221; Telepath says it will sacrifice growth and hire moderators who work in-house as long-term, trusted employees.</p>\n<p>&#8220;All the major social networks essentially grew in an unbounded way,&#8221; explains Henry. &#8220;They had 100 million-plus active users, then were like, &#8216;okay, now how do we moderate this enormous thing?&#8217;,&#8221; he continues. &#8220;We&#8217;re in a lucky position because we get to moderate from day one. We get to set the norms.&#8221;</p>\n<h2>Moderation</h2>\n<p>&#8220;Day one&#8221; was a long time in the making, however. The team rebuilt the product four times over a couple of years. Now, they say they&#8217;ve developed internal tools that provide moderators with visibility into the system.</p>\n<p>According to moderator head Estévez, these include a reporting system, real-time content streams organized in to buckets (e.g. a bucket for &#8220;only new users&#8221;), as well as various searchable ways to get context around a report or a particular problematic user.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Really good tools — including real-time streams of content, classifiers for problematic behavior, searchable context, and making it hard for banned users to return — mean that each moderator we hire will be quite scalable. We think that there are network effects around positive behavior,&#8221; she says.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2058471\" style=\"width: 324px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2058471\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2058471\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot2.png?w=314\" alt=\"\" width=\"314\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot2.png 1242w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot2.png?resize=69,150 69w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot2.png?resize=139,300 139w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot2.png?resize=768,1662 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot2.png?resize=314,680 314w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot2.png?resize=710,1536 710w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot2.png?resize=946,2048 946w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot2.png?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 314px) 100vw, 314px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2058471\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Telepath</p></div></p>\n<p>&#8220;It’s our intention to scale up fast and high accuracy moderation decision-making, which means that we’re going to be investing a lot of engineering effort in getting these tools right,&#8221; she adds.</p>\n<p>The founders have decided not to use any third-party systems to aid in moderation at this time, they told TechCrunch.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We looked at a bunch of off-the-shelf [moderation systems], and we&#8217;re basically building everything that we need from scratch,&#8221; says Henry. &#8220;We just need more control over being able to tweak how these systems work in order to get the outcome that we want.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The investment in human moderation over automation will also require additional capital to scale. And Telepath&#8217;s decision to not run ads means it will eventually need to consider alternative business models to sustain itself. The company, for now, is interested in subscriptions, but hasn&#8217;t made decisions on this front yet.</p>\n<h2>Banning the trolls</h2>\n<p>Though Telepath has only 4,000-plus users in its private beta, the two-person moderation team is already tasked with moderating posts from across the thousands of pieces of content shared on a daily basis. (The company doesn&#8217;t disclose how many violations it takes action against per day, on average.)</p>\n<p>When a user breaks the rules, moderators may first warn them about the violation and may require them to take down or edit a specific post. No one is punished for making a mistake or being unaware of the rules &#8212; they&#8217;re first given a chance to fix it.</p>\n<p>But if a user breaks the rules repeatedly or in a way that seems intentional, such as engaging in a harassment campaign around another user, they are banned entirely. Because of the phone number verification system, they also can&#8217;t easily return &#8212; unless they go out and purchase a new phone, that is.</p>\n<p>These moderation actions don&#8217;t necessarily have to follow strict guidelines, like a &#8220;three strikes rule,&#8221; for example. Instead, the way the rules may be enforced are determined on a case-by-case basis. Where Telepath leans towards stricter enforcement is around intentional and flagrant violations, or those where there&#8217;s a pattern of bad behavior. (As with <a href=\"https://mashable.com/article/twitter-reply-guys/\">Reply Guys</a> and <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sealioning\">sealioning</a> behavior.)</p>\n<p>In addition, unlike on Facebook and Twitter &#8212; platforms that sometimes seem to be caught off guard by viral trends in need of moderation &#8212; Telepath intends for nothing to go viral on its platform without having been seen by a human moderator, the company says.</p>\n<h2>Fake News</h2>\n<p>Telepath is also working to develop a reputation score for users and trust scores for publishers.</p>\n<p>In the case of the former, the goal is help the company determine how likely the user is to break Telepath&#8217;s rules. This isn&#8217;t developed yet, but would be something used behind the scenes, not put on display for all to see.</p>\n<p>For publishers, the trust score will be how factually correct they are what percentage of the time.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1512343\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1512343\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-1512343\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/fakenews.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/fakenews.jpg 2121w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/fakenews.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/fakenews.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/fakenews.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/fakenews.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/fakenews.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/fakenews.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/fakenews.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1512343\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> <a href=\"http://www.gettyimages.com/search/photographer?family=creative&#38;photographer=Thomas+Faull\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Thomas Faull <span class=\"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)</span></a> / Getty Images</p></div></p>\n<p>&#8220;For example, if the most popular article in terms of views from the publisher is just completely factually incorrect or intentionally misleading&#8230;that should have a bigger penalty on the trust score,&#8221; explains Henry. &#8220;The problem is that the incumbent platforms have rules against disinformation, but the problem is that they don&#8217;t enforce them out of this desire to appear balanced.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Bodnick adds this challenge is not as insurmountable as it seems.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Our view is that, actually, a handful of outlets are responsible for most of the disinformation&#8230;I don&#8217;t think our intent is to build out some modern-day truth system that will figure out if The Washington Post is slightly more accurate than The New York Times. I think the main goal will be to identify repeat disinformation publishers &#8212; determine that they are perpetual publishers of disinformation, and then crush their distribution,&#8221; says Bodnick.</p>\n<p>This plan, however, involves setting rules on Telepath that fly in the face of what many today consider &#8220;free speech.&#8221; In fact, Telepath&#8217;s position is that free speech-favoring social networks are a failed system.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The problem, in our view, is that when you take this free-speech centered approach that sort of says: &#8216;I don&#8217;t care how many disinformation posts Breitbart has published in the last &#8212; three years, three months, three weeks &#8212; we&#8217;re going to treat every new post as if it could be equally likely to be truthful as any other post in the system,'&#8221; says Bodnick. &#8220;That is inefficient.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;That&#8217;s how we will scale this disinformation rule &#8212; by determining which relatively small group of publishers &#8212; I&#8217;m guessing it&#8217;s hundreds, low hundreds &#8212; are responsible for publishing lots of disinformation. And then take their distribution down,&#8221; he says.</p>\n<p>This opinion on free speech is shared by the team.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We’re trying to build a community, which means that we have to make certain tradeoffs,&#8221; adds Estévez. &#8220;In the rules we refer to <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paradox_of_tolerance#:~:text=In%201945%2C%20philosopher%20Karl%20Popper,to%20the%20disappearance%20of%20tolerance.\">Karl Popper’s paradox of tolerance</a> — to maintain a tolerant society, you have to be intolerant of intolerance. We have no interest in giving a platform to certain kinds of speech,&#8221; she notes.</p>\n<p>This is the exact opposite approach that conservative social media sites are taking, like Parler and Gab. There, the companies believe in free speech to the point that they&#8217;ve <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2020/10/07/russian-trolls-graphika-parler-gab/\">left up content posted by an alleged Russian disinformation campaign,</a> saying that no one filed a report about the threat, and law enforcement hadn&#8217;t reached out. These MAGA-friendly social networks <a href=\"https://www.fastcompany.com/90522049/i-joined-parler-the-right-wing-echo-chambers-new-favorite-alt-twitter\">are also filled with</a> conspiracies, un-fact checked reports, and, frankly, a lot of vitriol.</p>\n<p>The expectation is that if you go on their platforms, you&#8217;re in charge of muting and blocking trolls or the content you don&#8217;t like. But by their nature, those who join these platforms will generally find themselves among like-minded users.</p>\n<p>Twitter, meanwhile, tries to straddle the middle ground. And in doing so, has alienated a number of users who think it doesn&#8217;t go far enough in counteracting abuse. Users report harassment and threats, then wait for days for their report to be reviewed only to be told the tweet in question didn&#8217;t break Twitter&#8217;s terms.</p>\n<p>Telepath sits on the other end of the spectrum, aggressively moderating content, blocking and banning users if needed, and punishing publications that don&#8217;t fact check or those that peddle misinformation.</p>\n<h2>&#8220;Kindness&#8221; carve-outs</h2>\n<p>And yet, despite all this extra effort, Telepath doesn&#8217;t always feature only thoughtful and kind-hearted conversations.</p>\n<p>That&#8217;s because it has carved out an exception in its kindness rule that allows users to criticize public figures, and because it doesn&#8217;t appear to be taking action on what could be problematic, if not violating, conversations.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2058470\" style=\"width: 324px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2058470\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2058470\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot3.png?w=314\" alt=\"\" width=\"314\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot3.png 1242w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot3.png?resize=69,150 69w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot3.png?resize=139,300 139w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot3.png?resize=768,1662 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot3.png?resize=314,680 314w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot3.png?resize=710,1536 710w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot3.png?resize=946,2048 946w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TelepathScreenshot3.png?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 314px) 100vw, 314px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2058470\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Telepath</p></div></p>\n<p>A user&#8217;s experience in these &#8220;gray&#8221; areas may vary by community.</p>\n<p>Telepath&#8217;s communities today focus on hobbies and interests, and can range from the innocuous &#8212; like Books or Branding or Netflix or Cooking, for example &#8212; to the potentially fraught, like Race in America. In the latter, there have been discussions about the capitalization of &#8220;Black&#8221; where it was suggested that maybe this wasn&#8217;t a useful idea. In another, sympathy is expressed for a person who was falsely <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/09/17/us/wisconsin-grad-student-race-trnd/index.html\">pretending</a> to be a person of color.</p>\n<p>In a post about affordable housing, someone openly wondered if a woman who said she didn&#8217;t want to live near poor people was actually racist. Another commenter then noted that gang members can bring down property values.</p>\n<p>A QAnon community, meanwhile, discusses the movement and its ridiculous followers from afar &#8212; which is apparently permitted &#8212; though supporting it in earnest would not be.</p>\n<p>There are also nearly 20 groups about things that &#8220;suck,&#8221; as in GOPSucks or CNNSucks or QuibiSucks.</p>\n<p>Anti-Trump content, meanwhile, can be found on a network called &#8220;DumbHitler.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, online publishers who routinely post discredited information are banned from Telepath, but YouTube is not. So if feel you need to share a link to a video of Rudy Giuliani accusing Biden of dementia, you can do so &#8212; so long as you don&#8217;t call it the truth.</p>\n<p>And you can post opinions about some terrible people in which you describe them as terrible, thanks to the public figure carve-out.</p>\n<p>Cheater and deadbeat dad? Go ahead and call them a &#8220;disgusting human being.&#8221; VP Pence was referred to by a commenter as &#8220;SmugFace mcWhitey&#8221; and Ronny Jackson is described as &#8220;such a piece of sh**.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Explains Estévez, that&#8217;s because Telepath&#8217;s &#8220;be kind” rule is not intended to protect public figures from criticism.</p>\n<p>&#8220;It is important to note that toxicity on the internet around politics isn’t because people are using bad words, but because people are using bad faith arguments. They are spreading misinformation. They are gaslighting marginalised groups about their experiences. These are the real issues we’re addressing,&#8221; she says.</p>\n<p>She also notes that online &#8220;civility&#8221; is often used to silence people from marginalized groups.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We don’t want Telepath’s focus on kindness to be turned against those who criticize powerful people,&#8221; she adds.</p>\n<p>In practice, the way this plays out on Telepath today is that it&#8217;s become a private, closed door network where users can bash Trump, his supporters and right-wing politicians in peace from Twitter trolls. And it&#8217;s a place where a majority agrees with those opinions, too.</p>\n<p>It has, then, seemingly built the Twitter that many on the left have wanted, the way that conservative social media, like Gab and Parler, built what the right had wanted. But in the end, it&#8217;s not clear if this is the solution for the problems of modern social media or merely an escape. It also remains to be seen whether a mainstream user base will follow.</p>\n<p>Telepath remains in a closed beta of indefinite length. You need an invite to join.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=07eFa-cWZHA:FOxnZiSKcKs:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Venture capital gets less diverse in 2020","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2058881","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Welcome back to The TechCrunch Exchange, a weekly startups-and-markets newsletter. It’s broadly based on </span></i><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/the-exchange/\"><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">the daily column that appears on Extra Crunch</span></i></a><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, but free, and made for your weekend reading. You can <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/newsletters\">subscribe here</a>.</span></i></p>\n<hr />\n<p>First, a big congrats on making it through the week. If you live in the United States, you just endured one of the wildest news weeks ever. Rapid-fire headlines and nigh-panic have been our lot since last Friday when the president announced he was COVID-19 positive. We’re all very tired. You get points for just surviving.</p>\n<p>Second, I wanted to bring you something uplifting this weekend, as you deserve it. Sadly, that’s not what we’re going to talk about.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>On Friday, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/funding-for-female-founders-falls-to-2017-levels-as-pandemic-shakes-up-the-vc-market/\">The Exchange covered new data</a> concerning the venture capital results of female founders during the third quarter. The data set was U.S.-focused, but we can presume that it is illustrative of global trends. Regardless of that nuance, the data was depressing.</p>\n<p>In the third quarter, U.S.-based female founders and co-founders raised 136 rounds worth $434 million, <a href=\"https://pitchbook.com/news/articles/vc-funding-female-founders-drops-low\">per PitchBook data</a>. That was a handful more rounds than Q2 2020, but far fewer dollars. And it was down across the board compared to Q3 2019. Even more, as we noted in the piece, the aggregate venture capital world did very well.</p>\n<p>Here’s <a href=\"https://www.pwc.com/us/en/industries/technology/moneytree.html\">some PwC data making that point</a>, and <a href=\"https://about.crunchbase.com/blog/the-monthly-rundown-startups-to-watch-from-shamus-the-sales-guy-september/?utm_source=twitter&#38;utm_medium=organic&#38;utm_campaign=evergreen&#38;utm_content=blog&#38;utm_term=sales\">a bit more from my old employer Crunchbase</a>. What matters is that female founders are doing worse when VCs are super active. This will only perpetuate inequalities and inequities in the startup market.</p>\n<p>Speaking of which, here’s some more bad news. <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/vdhjr/\">Vern Howard Jr.,</a> the co-founder and CEO of <a href=\"https://www.hallothere.com/\">Hallo</a>, a startup that has raised nearly $2 million, <a href=\"https://www.crunchbase.com/organization/hallo-348f/company_financials\">according to Crunchbase</a>, compiled some data on Black founders’ VC performance in Q3. Here’s <a href=\"https://medium.com/halloapp/hallo-research-black-founder-funding-cef159448b1e\">what he set out to do</a>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>[W]e wanted to put hard numbers behind the promises of so many venture capitalists and create a benchmark for how we can track the investment into black founders over time. So our team pulled a list from Crunchbase of all the startups globally with a total funding amount of $500,000 — $20,000,000 and who raised a round between July 1 and October 1. There were over 1383 companies here and our team went through one by one, to see how many Black founders there were.</p></blockquote>\n<p>There were 31.</p>\n<p>Now, you could open up the funding bands to include both smaller and larger funding events, but regardless of the data boundaries, the resulting number &#8212; just 2.2% of the total &#8212; is a disgrace.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"gVJdgdu0sy\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/funding-for-female-founders-falls-to-2017-levels-as-pandemic-shakes-up-the-vc-market/\">Funding for female founders falls to 2017 levels as pandemic shakes up the VC market</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Funding for female founders falls to 2017 levels as pandemic shakes up the VC market&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/funding-for-female-founders-falls-to-2017-levels-as-pandemic-shakes-up-the-vc-market/embed/#?secret=gVJdgdu0sy\" data-secret=\"gVJdgdu0sy\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<h2>Market Notes</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>The OpenDoor-SPAC deal became clearer this week as <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/a-quick-peek-into-opendoors-financial-results/\">we got a scratch at its financials</a>. Some of the data is rough. Some of it is good. But we can now understand the bull case for its future, which helps.</li>\n<li>Affirm announced that it has filed privately to go public, while Root filed publicly to go public. More on the Affirm news <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/affirm-files-confidentially-to-go-public/\">here</a> and a dig into <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/inside-roots-ipo-filing/\">the Root S-1 here</a>.</li>\n<li>Make sure to check out <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/ycharts-sells-to-pe-firm-in-all-cash-transaction-as-it-looks-to-pass-15m-arr-this-year/\">YCharts’ exit to a PE firm</a>. The startup told TechCrunch that it will pass $15 million in annual recurring revenue this year. Which should mean that it sold for a pretty penny.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.greycroft.com/\">Greycroft</a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/greycroft-has-rounded-up-678-million-in-capital-across-two-new-funds/\">raised an ocean of new capital</a>, to the tune of $678 million spread between a $310 million fund for early-stage checks, and a $368 million fund targeting growth-stage deals.</li>\n<li>Why do we care about Greycroft? We don’t, per se, but it is worth noting that VCs are still able to raise during the current crisis. We <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/12/doing-deals-through-zoom-these-investors-have-some-tips/\">often talk about how founders are managing to raise during COVID</a>, and this is something that VCs have to do, as well.</li>\n<li>TechCrunch <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/investors-founders-report-hot-market-for-api-startups/\">dug into the API startup space</a>, talking to VCs and founders alike about the space and why it’s blowing up in 2020.</li>\n<li>Airbnb’s summer was painful, but its rebound may prove legendary. The Exchange <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/understanding-airbnbs-summer-recovery/\">examined how it managed to bounce back so quickly</a>.</li>\n<li>And finally, from Market Notes, some rounds that you should not miss: <a href=\"https://zira.ai/\">Zira.ai</a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/07/zira-raises-3-1m-for-its-shift-scheduling-service-that-helps-manage-hourly-workers/\">raised $3.1 million</a>, <a href=\"https://www.grid.ai/\">Grid AI</a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/grid-ai-raises-18-6m-series-a-to-help-ai-researchers-and-engineers-bring-their-models-to-production/\">raised $18.6 million to help machine learning devs do more</a>, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/instacart-raises-200m-more-at-17-7b-valuation/\">Instacart raised $200 million more at a valuation of nearly $18 billion</a>, <a href=\"https://www.mmhmm.app/\">mmhmm</a> <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/alexkonrad/2020/10/07/video-startup-mmhmm-raises-31-million-pre-launch/#26072ad2bcc2\">raised $21 million in the best-named round of the week</a>, <a href=\"https://www.unqork.com/\">Unqork</a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/07/unqorks-207m-series-c-underscores-growing-enterprise-demand-for-no-code-apps/\">raised $207 million and we dug into what that means for the no-code market</a>, and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/gopuff-funding/\">GoPuff raised $380 million more in an epic round that values the delivery startup at $3.9 billion</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"CE1nMIboS1\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/ycharts-sells-to-pe-firm-in-all-cash-transaction-as-it-looks-to-pass-15m-arr-this-year/\">YCharts sells to PE firm in all-cash transaction as it looks to pass $15M ARR this year</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;YCharts sells to PE firm in all-cash transaction as it looks to pass $15M ARR this year&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/ycharts-sells-to-pe-firm-in-all-cash-transaction-as-it-looks-to-pass-15m-arr-this-year/embed/#?secret=CE1nMIboS1\" data-secret=\"CE1nMIboS1\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<h2>Various and Sundry</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Continuing our coverage of <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/17/saving-not-spending-is-the-new-hotness-in-fintech/\">the savings and investing boom</a> that fintech startups <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/18/fintechs-savings-and-investing-boom-isnt-just-a-domestic-affair/%5C\">around the world have been riding this year</a>, <a href=\"https://freetrade.io/\">Freetrade</a>, a British Robinhood if you will, told The Exchange that it crossed £1 billion in September order volume. That’s not bad!</li>\n<li>Freetrade also recently launched a paid version of its service, as the payment-for-order-flow method of generating revenue <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/06/robinhoods-q2-revenue-appears-to-soar/\">that Robinhood is growing on the back of</a> is not allowed across the pond.</li>\n<li>Sticking to the fintech world, <a href=\"https://www.withyotta.com/\">Yotta Savings</a> is a startup that provides a savings option to its users, with the added chance of winning a big monetary prize for having stored their money with the startup. Folks have been whispering in my ear about the company for a bit, but I’ve held off writing about it until now as it was not clear to me if the model was merely a gimmick, or something that would actually attract customers.</li>\n<li>Well, Yotta grew from 8,000 accounts to more than 30,000 in the past few weeks and has reached the $100 million deposit mark. So, I guess we now care.</li>\n<li>Coinbase <a href=\"https://blog.coinbase.com/a-follow-up-to-coinbase-as-a-mission-focused-company-6e7545e9aea2\">lost one in 20 employees</a> to its new strategy of standing neutral during political times on anything that its CEO deems as unrelated to its core mission, which, as a for-profit company with tectonic financial backing, is making money.</li>\n<li>On the same topic, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/can\">Can</a> from <a href=\"https://twitter.com/readmargins\">The Margins</a> <a href=\"https://themargins.substack.com/p/all-politics-is-bad-says-coinbase?utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=cta\">made a salient point</a> that “no politics is a political stance.” Correct, and it is a very conservative one at that.</li>\n<li>Even more, Coinbase’s CEO <a href=\"https://blog.coinbase.com/coinbase-is-a-mission-focused-company-af882df8804\">made noise</a> about how his company will “work to create an environment where everyone is welcome and can do their best work, regardless of background, sexual orientation, race, gender, age, etc.” Whether he likes it or not, this is a political stance, and one that has nothing to do with the company’s stated core mission. And a political fight earned it &#8212; namely, equal access to the workplace.</li>\n<li>I’ll toss in a plug for <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/01/working-for-social-justice-isnt-a-distraction-for-mission-focused-companies/\">this piece on the matter</a> from a VC that TechCrunch published, and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/01/working-for-social-justice-isnt-a-distraction-for-mission-focused-companies/\">these thoughts</a> from a tech denizen on how to guarantee that your company lands on the wrong side of history on essentially everything.</li>\n<li>Wrapping our grab-bag this week, <a href=\"https://seekingalpha.com/pr/18034189-ping-identity-acquires-personal-identity-leader-shocard-to-revolutionize-privacy-streamline\">Ping Identity bought ShoCard</a>. Ping is now a public company, so normally its deals would land outside our wheelhouse. But we care in this case because TechCrunch has covered ShoCard (2015: “<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2015/05/05/shocard-is-a-digital-identity-card-on-the-blockchain/#:~:text=Romain%20Dillet%40romaindillet%20%2F%202%3A,identity%20whenever%20you%20need%20to.\">ShoCard Is A Digital Identity Card On The Blockchain</a>”), and because the startup does crypto-related work.</li>\n<li>Seeing a public company snap up a blockchain startup for real money, on purpose and out loud, doesn’t happen every day. More <a href=\"https://www.eweek.com/security/why-ping-identity-s-acquisition-of-shocard-may-preview-future-of-security\">here</a> if you want to read about the deal.</li>\n</ul>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Dan8vuxo9S\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/01/working-for-social-justice-isnt-a-distraction-for-mission-focused-companies/\">Working for social justice isn&#8217;t a &#8216;distraction&#8217; for mission-focused companies</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Working for social justice isn&#8217;t a &#8216;distraction&#8217; for mission-focused companies&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/01/working-for-social-justice-isnt-a-distraction-for-mission-focused-companies/embed/#?secret=Dan8vuxo9S\" data-secret=\"Dan8vuxo9S\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Wrapping, this newsletter is a lot of fun and I appreciate your reading it. It is, also, a work in progress. So feel free to hit respond to it and let me know what you want to see more of. Or hit respond and send me a cute pic of your pet. Either is fine by me.</p>\n<p>Chat soon,</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/alex\">Alex</a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/SxINyvtnSf4\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sat, 10 Oct 2020 20:00:54 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"be727f6479511da192ce71da5eb97635","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn21@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-34-245_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Alex Wilhelm","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn21@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-34-245_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn43@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-47-798_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn73@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-46-413_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=SxINyvtnSf4:zZsZKFlEEcM:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn23@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-04-46-527_18e363e601577932.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=SxINyvtnSf4:zZsZKFlEEcM:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn97@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-46-451_d93bee14d6bc0f2b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn77@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-48-385_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/SxINyvtnSf4":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn56@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-46-402_e24ac820e451877e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522266665},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Snapdocs raises $60M to manage the mortgage process in the cloud","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059134","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">The U.S. economy may be in a precarious state right now, with a presidential election looming on the horizon and the country still in the grips of the coronavirus pandemic. But partly thanks to lower interest rates, the housing market <a href=\"https://www.census.gov/construction/nrs/pdf/newressales.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">continues to rise</a>, and today a startup that has built technology to help it run more efficiently is announcing a major growth round of funding. </span></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://snapdocs.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Snapdocs</a>, which is used by some 130,000 real estate professionals to digitally manage the mortgage process and other paperwork and stages related to buying a home, has raised $60 million in new equity funding on the heels of a few bullish months of business.</p>\n<p>In August 2020 &#8212; a peak in home sales in the U.S., reaching their highest level in 14 years &#8212; the startup saw 170,000 home sales, totaling some $50 million in transactions, closed on its platform. This accounted for almost 15% of all deals done that month in the U.S. <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/snapdocs\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"snapdocs\">Snapdocs <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> is now on track to close 1.5 million deals this year, double its 2019 volume.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>On top of this, the startup&#8217;s platform is being used by more than 70% of settlement agents nationally, with customers including Bell Bank, LeaderOne Financial Corporation, Googain and Georgia United Credit Union among its customers.</p>\n<p>The Series C is being led by YC Continuity (Snapdocs was part of Y Combinator&#8217;s Winter 2014 cohort), with existing investors Sequoia Capital, F-Prime Capital and Founders Fund, and new backers Lachy Groom (<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/10/03/elements-stripes-new-check-out-toolkit-aims-to-boost-e-commerce-sales-completions/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">formerly of Stripe</a> and now a prolific investor) and DocuSign, a strategic backer, also participating.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Like us they are on a mission to defragment an ecosystem,&#8221; King said, referring to it as a &#8220;perfect complement&#8221; to Snapdocs&#8217; own efforts.</p>\n<p>Snapdocs is not talking about its valuation. Aaron King, the founder and CEO, said in an interview that he believes disclosing it is nothing more than &#8220;grandstanding&#8221; &#8212; which is interesting considering that the industry he focuses on, real estate, is all about public disclosures of valuation &#8212; but he noted that most of the $103 million that the startup has raised to date is still in the bank, which says something about the company&#8217;s overall financial health.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ZMdm4Dm6Bd\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/10/zumper-raises-60m-to-double-down-on-tech-to-grow-its-apartment-rentals-platform/\">Zumper raises $60M to double down on tech to grow its apartment rentals platform</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Zumper raises $60M to double down on tech to grow its apartment rentals platform&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/10/zumper-raises-60m-to-double-down-on-tech-to-grow-its-apartment-rentals-platform/embed/#?secret=ZMdm4Dm6Bd\" data-secret=\"ZMdm4Dm6Bd\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>And for some further context, according to <a href=\"https://my.pitchbook.com/profile/63692-65/company/profile\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">PitchBook</a> data estimates, Snapdocs was valued at $200 million in its last round, in October 2019.</p>\n<p>Snapdocs&#8217; central premise is that buying a house requires not just a lot of paperwork but also a lot of different parties to be on the same page, so to speak, to set the wheels in motion and get a deal done. There is not just the mortgage (with its multiple parties) to settle; you also have real estate brokers and agents, the home sellers, inspectors and appraisers, the insurance company, the title company and more &#8212; some 15 parties in all.</p>\n<p>The complexity of all of them working together in a quick and efficient way often means the process of buying and selling a house can be long and costly. And that&#8217;s before the pandemic &#8212; with the problems associated with social distancing and remote working &#8212; hit us.</p>\n<p>Snapdocs&#8217; solution has been to build one platform in the cloud that helps to manage the documents needed by all of these different parties, providing access to data and the ability to flag or approve things remotely, to speed the process along. It also has built a number of features, using AI technology and analytics, to also help identify what might be potential issues early on and get them fixed.</p>\n<p>King is not your typical tech startup entrepreneur. He began working in mortgages as a notary when he was still in high school &#8212; he&#8217;s effectively been in the industry for 23 years, he said &#8212; and his earliest startup efforts were focused on one aspect of the complexities that he knew first-hand: he saw an opportunity to lean on technology to get notarized signatures sorted out in a legal, orderly and quicker way.</p>\n<p>He then got deeper into identifying the possibilities of how tech could be used to improve the larger process, and that is how Snapdocs came into existence.</p>\n<p>Given how big the real estate market is &#8212; it&#8217;s the largest asset class in the world, by many estimates &#8212; and how many other industries tech has &#8220;disrupted&#8221; over the years, it&#8217;s interesting that there have been so few attempting to solve it. One of the reasons, it seems, is that there hasn&#8217;t been enough of a crossover between tech experts and mortgage experts, and Snapdocs is a testament to the virtues of building a startup specifically around a hard problem that you happen to know really well.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Most people have identified this as a tech problem, and a lot of the tech &#8212; such as e-signatures &#8212; has existed for 20 years, but the fragmentation of real estate is the issue,&#8221; he said. &#8220;We&#8217;re talking about a mass constellation of companies and workflow. But we&#8217;re obsessed about the workflow of all of these constituents.&#8221;</p>\n<p>That&#8217;s a position that has helped Snapdocs build its standing with the industry, as well as with investors.</p>\n<p>“I’ve known the Snapdocs team for many years and have always been amazed by their focus and execution toward bringing each stakeholder in the mortgage process online,” said Anu Hariharan, partner at YC Continuity, in a statement. “In 2013, Snapdocs began as a notary marketplace before expanding horizontally to service title companies and, more recently, lenders. By connecting the numerous parties involved in a mortgage on a single platform, Snapdocs is quickly becoming the “operating system” for mortgage closings. Mortgages, much like commerce, will shift online, bringing improved efficiency and a far better customer experience to the outdated home-closing process.” Hariharan has real estate experience herself and is joining the board with this round.</p>\n<p>There have been a number of companies taking new, tech-based approaches to the market to find new and faster ways of doing things, and to open up new kinds of value in the market.</p>\n<p>Opendoor, for example, has rethought the whole process of selling and buying houses, taking on a role as a middleman in the process both to take on a lot of the harder work of fixing up a home, and handling all of the difficult stages in the sales process: it&#8217;s a role that has recently seen the company <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/opendoor-to-go-public-by-way-of-chamath-palihapitiya-spac/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">catapult to a valuation of $4.8 billion</a> by way of a SPAC-based public listing. An interesting idea, King said, but still only accounting for a small sliver of house sales.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"nLP4wUavzS\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/opendoor-to-go-public-by-way-of-chamath-palihapitiya-spac/\">Opendoor to go public by way of Chamath Palihapitiya SPAC</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Opendoor to go public by way of Chamath Palihapitiya SPAC&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/opendoor-to-go-public-by-way-of-chamath-palihapitiya-spac/embed/#?secret=nLP4wUavzS\" data-secret=\"nLP4wUavzS\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Others, like <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/10/orchard-real-estate-platform-raises-69-million-series-c-led-by-revolution-growth/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Orchard</a>, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/11/07/reonomy-a-massive-database-of-commercial-property-intel-raises-60m/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Reonomy</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/10/zumper-raises-60m-to-double-down-on-tech-to-grow-its-apartment-rentals-platform/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Zumper</a>, have all also raised large rounds on the back of a lot of promise of the market continuing to grow and the opportunity to take part in that process through new approaches. It&#8217;s a sign that &#8220;safe as houses&#8221; still has a place in the market, even with all the other unknowns in play.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Over the next five years the real estate industry will be completely digitized, so a lot of companies are trying to figure out what their place are, and how to provide value,&#8221; King said.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Lunden","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn21@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-34-245_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn43@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-47-798_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn73@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-46-413_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Ml1pwKR1STI:9cp1wrjGa6M:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn47@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-46-405_2d1f99d436f16fe9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Ml1pwKR1STI:9cp1wrjGa6M:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn97@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-48-516_ea07c775f5913bb4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn77@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-48-385_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/Ml1pwKR1STI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn96@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-46-447_bb91ed343719acbe.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522266666},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Twilio is buying customer data startup Segment for between $3B and $4B","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059035","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Sources have told TechCrunch that <a href=\"http://twilio.com\">Twilio</a> intends to acquire customer data startup <a href=\"http://segment.com\">Segment</a> for between $3 and $4 billion. <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-segment-m-a-twilio/twilio-to-buy-cloud-customer-data-startup-segment-for-3-2-billion-forbes-idUSKBN26V033\">Forbes</a> broke the story on Friday night, reporting a price tag of $3.2 billion.</p>\n<p>We have heard from a couple of industry sources that the deal is in the works and could be announced as early as Monday.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/twilio\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"twilio\">Twilio <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Segment are both API companies. That means they create an easy way for developers to tap into a specific type of functionality without writing a lot of code. As I wrote in a 2017 article on <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/segment-io\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"segment-io\">Segment, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/11/16/segment-has-a-plan-to-help-companies-comply-with-gdpr-data-privacy-requests/\">it provides a set of APIs </a>to pull together customer data from a variety of sources:</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<blockquote><p>Segment has made a name for itself by providing a set of APIs that enable it to gather data about a customer from a variety of sources like your CRM tool, customer service application and website and pull that all together into a single view of the customer, something that is the goal of every company in the customer information business.</p></blockquote>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"f67q9X61N4\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/11/16/segment-has-a-plan-to-help-companies-comply-with-gdpr-data-privacy-requests/\">Segment has a plan to help companies comply with GDPR data privacy requests</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Segment has a plan to help companies comply with GDPR data privacy requests&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/11/16/segment-has-a-plan-to-help-companies-comply-with-gdpr-data-privacy-requests/embed/#?secret=f67q9X61N4\" data-secret=\"f67q9X61N4\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>While Twilio&#8217;s main focus since it launched in 2008 has been on making it easy to embed communications functionality into any app, it signaled a switch in direction when it released the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/03/12/twilio-launches-flex-a-fully-programmable-contact-center/\">Flex customer service API</a> in March 2018. Later that same year, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/15/twilio-acquires-email-api-platform-sendgrid-for-2-billion-in-stock/\">it bought SendGrid</a>, an email marketing API company for $2 billion.</p>\n<p>Twilio&#8217;s market cap as of Friday <a href=\"https://www.google.com/search?q=twilio+stock&#38;oq=twilio+stock&#38;aqs=chrome..69i57j0l6j69i60.4457j1j1&#38;sourceid=chrome&#38;ie=UTF-8\">was an impressive $45 billion</a>. You could see how it can afford to flex its financial muscles to combine Twilio&#8217;s core API mission, especially Flex, with the ability to pull customer data with Segment and create customized email or <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/06/twilio-launches-sendgrid-ads-and-new-cross-channel-messaging-api/\">ads</a> with SendGrid.</p>\n<p>This could enable Twilio to expand beyond pure core communications capabilities and it could come at the cost of around $5 billion for the two companies, a good deal for what could turn out to be a substantial business as more and more companies look for ways to understand and communicate with their customers in more relevant ways across multiple channels.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"5PJMYQRV17\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/03/12/twilio-launches-flex-a-fully-programmable-contact-center/\">Twilio launches Flex, a fully programmable contact center</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Twilio launches Flex, a fully programmable contact center&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/03/12/twilio-launches-flex-a-fully-programmable-contact-center/embed/#?secret=5PJMYQRV17\" data-secret=\"5PJMYQRV17\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>As Semil Shah from early stage VC firm Haystack <a href=\"https://semilshah.com/2020/10/10/quickly-unpacking-twilios-3-2b-acquisition-of-segment/\">wrote in the company blog yesterday</a>, Segment saw a different way to gather customer data, and Twilio was wise to swoop in and buy it.</p>\n<blockquote><p>Segment’s belief was that a traditional CRM wasn’t robust enough for the enterprise to properly manage its pipe. Segment entered to provide customer data infrastructure to offer a more unified experience. Now under the Twilio umbrella, Segment can continue to build key integrations (like they have for Twilio data), which is being used globally inside Fortune 500 companies already.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Segment was founded in 2011 and raised over $283 million, according to Crunchbase data. Its most <a href=\"https://news.crunchbase.com/news/segment-raises-175m-for-big-data-infra/\">recent raise was $175 million</a> in April on a $1.5 billion valuation.</p>\n<p>Twilio stock closed at $306.24 per share on Friday up $2.39%.</p>\n<p><em>Segment declined to comment on this story. We also sent a request for comment to Twilio, but hadn&#8217;t heard back by the time we published.  If that changes, we will update the story.</em></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Nwpiw29AVm\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/15/twilio-acquires-email-api-platform-sendgrid-for-2-billion-in-stock/\">Twilio acquires email API platform SendGrid for $2 billion in stock</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Twilio acquires email API src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/15/twilio-acquires-email-api-platform-sendgrid-for-2-billion-in-stock/embed/#?secret=Nwpiw29AVm\" data-secret=\"Nwpiw29AVm\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Facebook EU-US data transfer complaint: Schrems gets a judicial review of the Irish DPC’s procedure","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059173","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Another twist in a multi-year complaint saga related to the legality of <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/facebook\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"facebook\">Facebook&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> data transfers: European privacy campaigner Max Schrems has today been granted a judicial review of the Irish regulator&#8217;s handling of his complaint.</p>\n<p>He&#8217;s expecting the hearing to take place before the end of the year &#8212; and is hoping the action will, at long last, lead to a suspension of Facebook&#8217;s EU-US data transfers.</p>\n<p>Schrems says his aim is to &#8220;kick start a &#8216;paused&#8217; complaints procedure'&#8221; after Ireland&#8217;s Data Protection Commission (DPC) chose to open a new case procedure last month &#8212; simultaneously pausing its handling of his original complaint, which dates back some seven years at this point.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The vintage complaint had a major injection of attention following a ruling by Europe&#8217;s top court <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/16/europes-top-court-strikes-down-flagship-eu-us-data-transfer-mechanism/\">this summer</a>, which struck down a flagship EU-US data transfer arrangement (called Privacy Shield) &#8212; and cast doubt on the legality of alternative transfer mechanisms for taking EU citizens&#8217; data to the U.S. for processing when processors are subject to U.S. surveillance law, as Facebook is.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ydpvJbllwZ\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/16/europes-top-court-strikes-down-flagship-eu-us-data-transfer-mechanism/\">Europe&#8217;s top court strikes down flagship EU-US data transfer mechanism</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Europe&#8217;s top court strikes down flagship EU-US data transfer mechanism&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/16/europes-top-court-strikes-down-flagship-eu-us-data-transfer-mechanism/embed/#?secret=ydpvJbllwZ\" data-secret=\"ydpvJbllwZ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Yet there&#8217;s still no decision on Schrems&#8217; original complaint. Hence, he&#8217;s returned to court.</p>\n<p>“The DPC has already pledged to the Court in 2015 that it will swiftly decide. It seems like we need a clear judgment to force the DPC to do its job,&#8221; said Schrems in a statement today on the judicial review being granted.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"><a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/SchremsII?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#SchremsII</a>: Irish High Court just granted leave to have a Juridical Review against the <a href=\"https://twitter.com/DPCIreland?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@DPCIreland</a> &#8212; to kick start the &#34;paused&#34; complaints procedure that should stop Facebook&#39;s EU-US data transfer (and clarifly crucial procedural issues)&#8230; <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.0/72x72/1f603.png\" alt=\"😃\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><a href=\"https://t.co/yMIyhonBaS\">https://t.co/yMIyhonBaS</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/max-schrems\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"max-schrems\">Max Schrems <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.0/72x72/1f1ea-1f1fa.png\" alt=\"🇪🇺\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.0/72x72/1f1e6-1f1f9.png\" alt=\"🇦🇹\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /> (@maxschrems) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/maxschrems/status/1315625962516680705?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 12, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<p>Facebook has already successfully applied for a judicial review of a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/09/facebook-told-it-may-have-to-suspend-eu-data-transfers-after-schrems-ii-ruling/\">preliminary order sent by the DPC last month</a> to suspend its data transfers to the U.S. The tech giant was granted a stay on that preliminary order, so its data transfers continue unabated and uninterrupted &#8212; even as the regulatory process is mired in yet more legal wrangling.</p>\n<p>The stay also bought Facebook more time to lobby EU lawmakers to &#8220;fix&#8221; the legal uncertainty now firmly attached to EU-U.S. data transfers &#8212; with <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/facebook-denies-it-will-pull-service-in-europe-over-data-transfer-ban/\">VP Nick Clegg popping up on a live-streamed debate last month</a> to predict economic doom for the region&#8217;s small businesses if Facebook gets forced to suspend transfers. (Clegg further claimed Facebook&#8217;s business of &#8220;personalized advertising&#8221; would be vital to Europe&#8217;s coronavirus economic recovery, without pointing out other, less invasive/rights-hostile forms of ad-targeting are available&#8230;)</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s not hard to see why Schrems is so unhappy that his 2013 complaint has been turned into an endless game of regulatory whack-a-mole that leaves Facebook free to continue its data-mining business as usual.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"OTyARq7AI8\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/25/max-schrems-on-the-eu-court-ruling-that-could-cut-facebook-in-two/\">Max Schrems on the EU court ruling that could cut Facebook in two</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Max Schrems on the EU court ruling that could cut Facebook in two&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/25/max-schrems-on-the-eu-court-ruling-that-could-cut-facebook-in-two/embed/#?secret=OTyARq7AI8\" data-secret=\"OTyARq7AI8\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>In a press release put out by his privacy-focused not-for-profit, <a href=\"https://noyb.eu/en/irish-high-court-allows-judicial-review-stop-facebook-eu-us-transfers\">noyb</a>, Schrems writes: &#8220;Today’s Judicial Review by <em>noyb</em> is in many ways the counterpart to Facebook’s Judicial Review: While Facebook wants to block the second procedure by the DPC, <em>noyb</em> wants to move the original complaints procedure towards a decision.&#8221;</p>\n<p>“The DPC has opened a second case, just get rid of the complainant from the first case. Now this second case was stalled by a lawsuit from Facebook within weeks. This was complete procedural mismanagement by the Irish regulator. We are now trying to kick start the original procedure from 2013 to finally get a decision by the DPC after seven years and five court judgements that all confirmed our position,&#8221; he adds in the statement.</p>\n<p>Schrems/noyb is also making a more pointed allegation against the regulator, saying it saw documents last week that suggest Facebook has been using alternative data transfer mechanisms to take EU users&#8217; data to the U.S. &#8212; and accusing the regulator of knowing about this since 2016, yet failing to pass the information on to it.</p>\n<p>“The documents we received suggest that seven years of procedures and both references to the European Court of Justice were largely irrelevant for the case before the DPC,&#8221; writes Schrems, accusing the regulator of hiding documents from the Courts and his lawyers &#8220;despite our right to be provided with all the files of a case&#8221;. &#8220;We are therefore asking the High Court to clarify that all documents must be put on the table that all parties are properly heard and a quick decision is then made,” he adds.</p>\n<p>We reached out to the DPC with questions but the regulator declined to answer specific points at this stage. “As you can see Mr Schrems’ application to the Court this morning was made ex parte, meaning that any comments/arguments put forward were unchallenged. We will outline our position when we make our own submission to the Court,&#8221; deputy commissioner, Graham Doyle, told us.</p>\n<p>Ireland&#8217;s regulator is no stranger to accusations of dragging its feet on enforcing the bloc&#8217;s data protection regime against major tech firms and platforms, many of whom have chosen to site their regional base in the country &#8212; meaning their data handling typically comes under the supervision of the DPC. (Which in turn means it has a huge backlog of complex, cross-border cases to investigate and issue decisions on.)</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"QGDcsbCreA\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/facebook-denies-it-will-pull-service-in-europe-over-data-transfer-ban/\">Facebook denies it will pull service in Europe over data transfer ban</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook denies it will pull service in Europe over data transfer ban&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/facebook-denies-it-will-pull-service-in-europe-over-data-transfer-ban/embed/#?secret=QGDcsbCreA\" data-secret=\"QGDcsbCreA\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>More than two years after the GDPR came into application, the DPC has only submitted one draft decision on cross-border cases (<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/20/further-delay-to-gdpr-enforcement-of-2018-twitter-breach/\">related to a Twitter security breach</a>) &#8212; which is still pending agreement from the EU&#8217;s other data supervisors.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/02/19/lack-of-big-tech-gdpr-decisions-looms-large-in-eu-watchdogs-annual-report/\">Scores more cases remain open on its desk</a>.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/24/gdprs-two-year-review-flags-lack-of-vigorous-enforcement/\">In June</a>, a Commission two-year review of GDPR flagged a lack of uniformly vigorous enforcement &#8212; with lawmakers acknowledging: “The best answer [to criticism of GDPR&#8217;s failure to regulate big tech] will be a decision from the Irish data protection authority about important cases.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Separately, Irish parliamentarian Malcolm Byrne raised questions in the senate recently over another long-standing complaint that&#8217;s sitting on the DPC&#8217;s desk &#8212; related to Google and the real-time bidding process that&#8217;s involved in programmatic advertising &#8212; also still an open investigation.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Today, I raised the issue of Google’s <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/RealTimeBidding?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#RealTimeBidding</a> system and again how big tech is using our data. cities.</p>\n<p>Our &#60;a href=&#8221;https://forms.gle/k4Ji2Ch7zdrn7o2p6”>survey of VCs in Lisbon will capture how the city is faring, and what changes are being wrought amongst investors by the coronavirus pandemic. (Please note, if you have filled the survey out already, there is no need to do it again).</p>\n<p>We’d like to know how Lisbon&#8217;s startup scene is evolving, how the tech sector is being impacted by COVID-19, and, generally, how your thinking will evolve from here.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Our survey will only be about investors, and <strong>only the contributions of VC investors will be included.</strong> More than one partner is welcome to fill out the survey.</p>\n<p>The shortlist of questions will require only brief responses, but the more you can add, the better.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://forms.gle/k4Ji2Ch7zdrn7o2p6\"><strong>You can fill out the survey here.</strong></a></p>\n<p>Obviously, investors who contribute will be featured in the final surveys, with links to their companies and profiles.</p>\n<p>What kinds of things do we want to know? Questions include: Which trends are you most excited by? What startup do you wish someone would create? Where are the overlooked opportunities? What are you looking for in your next investment, in general? How is your local ecosystem going? And how has COVID-19 impacted your investment strategy?</p>\n<p>This survey is part of a broader <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/extra-crunch/investor-surveys/\">series of surveys</a> we’re doing to help founders find the right investors.</p>\n<p>https://techcrunch.com/extra-crunch/investor-surveys/</p>\n<p>For example, here is the recent <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/09/14-vcs-discuss-covid-19-and-londons-future-as-a-tech-hub/\">survey of London</a>.</p>\n<p>You are not in Lisbon, but would like to take part? Or you are in another part of the country? That&#8217;s fine! Any European VC investor can STILL fill out the survey, as we probably will be putting a call out to your city next anyway! And we will use the data for future surveys on vertical topics.</p>\n<p>The survey is covering almost every European country on the continent of Europe (not just EU members, btw), so just look for your country and city on the <a href=\"https://forms.gle/k4Ji2Ch7zdrn7o2p6\">survey</a> and please participate (<em>if</em> you&#8217;re a venture capital investor).</p>\n<p>Thank you for participating.
