01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"Amazon launches an AR app that works with new QR codes on its boxes","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059196","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/amazon\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"amazon\">Amazon <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> has quietly launched a new augmented reality application that works with QR codes on the company&#8217;s shipping boxes to create &#8220;interactive, shareable&#8221; AR experiences. Called simply &#8220;<a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/id1519505870#?platform=iphone\">Amazon Augmented Reality,</a>&#8221; the retailer describes the app as a &#8220;fun way to reuse your Amazon boxes until you&#8217;re ready to drop them in the recycling bin.&#8221;</p>\n<p>As shown in the App Store&#8217;s screenshots of the new app, different Amazon boxes will offer unique activities for the AR experience. For example, one screenshot shows someone drawing the face on a pre-printed white pumpkin to turn it into a jack-o-lantern. When they then scan the QR code, the pumpkin jumps out as an AR object. Another screenshot shows an AR pumpkin and bat wings over top an image of a dog. And one shows the Amazon box turning into a little blue AR car when the QR code is scanned.</p>\n<p>In the accompanying App Store video, there are other animated characters, including the Amazon smile logo itself an an AR corgi dog that jumps out playfully when the QR code is scanned.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The company notes in the description that if your iPhone is also capable of TrueDepth technology, the app can also use the device&#8217;s camera to track your facial movements to enable features like a &#8220;selfie&#8221; mode.</p>\n<p>The app, which debuted a few days ago on the <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/id1519505870#?platform=iphone\">iOS App Store</a> and <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.Amazon.AmazonAR\">Google Play</a>, offers no other functionality if not used alongside an Amazon box that supports the new QR codes. (However, you can <a href=\"https://amazonar.app/getabox_halloween\">test out the experience here</a> if you don&#8217;t have a box to use.)</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059265\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2059265\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2059265\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-11.11.15-AM.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"281\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-11.11.15-AM.jpg 1952w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-11.11.15-AM.jpg?resize=150,62 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-11.11.15-AM.jpg?resize=300,124 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-11.11.15-AM.jpg?resize=768,317 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-11.11.15-AM.jpg?resize=680,281 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-11.11.15-AM.jpg?resize=1536,634 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-12-at-11.11.15-AM.jpg?resize=50,21 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2059265\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits: Amazon</strong></p></div></p>\n<p>At launch, however, the app appears to focus only on the pumpkin AR experience. Once you have designed and scanned your pumpkin into AR, you can then press other buttons to decorate the pumpkin further &#8212; by giving it a hat or outfit, changing its light or color, among other things. You can also flip the camera around to display the pumpkin on your selfie image, where it moves along with your face.  You can then press the Camera button in the app to snap a photo of your creation to share on social media.</p>\n<p>The new QR code-enabled boxes are only beginning to roll out now, so you may not have received one just yet, we understand. The boxes are also made using less material, as part of Amazon&#8217;s ongoing &#8220;Less Packaging, More Smiles&#8221; campaign.</p>\n<p><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/UTnjUxQNZsc?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<p>Amazon has been dabbling in AR for some time, most recently with the launch of <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/25/amazon-rolls-out-a-new-ar-shopping-feature-for-viewing-multiple-items-at-once/\">a new AR shopping feature</a> that allows users of its main Amazon shopping app to visualized multiple items of furniture or decor in their room at the same time. A few years ago, it had also launched a simpler version of AR shopping with <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/11/01/amazon-adds-an-ar-shopping-feature-to-its-ios-app/\">a feature called AR View in its Amazon iOS app</a>, built using ARKit.  It had also <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/05/24/amazon-adds-shoppable-stickers-to-its-ios-app/?_ga=2.163930047.1634671527.1598275068-508606782.1595599686\">once tried out “shoppable stickers” that used AR</a> to place basic stickers of products in your space, instead of realistic representations of the items.</p>\n<p>With its latest launch of the AR View feature, however, Amazon had done the work to support Apple&#8217;s latest version of ARKit and likely wanted to experiment further with the possibilities. The box-scanning AR app could serve as a way to test consumer demand for more AR products. But Amazon doesn&#8217;t appear to be using this app to collect extensive research data. The App Store description notes that all the information processed using the new technology in Amazon&#8217;s new AR Player will remain on the device, and is not &#8220;stored, processed or shared by Amazon.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The app is currently available on <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/id1519505870#?platform=iphone\">iOS</a> and <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.Amazon.AmazonAR\">Android</a> as a free download.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 01:04:26","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:26","title":"What to expect from Apple’s ‘Hi Speed’ iPhone event","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059295","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">For starters, iPhones, of course. That one was easy. The company skipped out on new mobile devices during its recent <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/apple\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"apple\">Apple <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Watch event, owing to COVID-19-related delays. And, of course, the fact that the events are all pre-taped and virtual now means companies can more easily split them up in ways that were harder to justify when people were expected to fly in from all over the world.</p>\n<p>That doesn’t mean we won’t be getting more than just a phone (or, more like multiple phones). While Apple’s been more inclined to host more, smaller events, there’s a decent chance this is going to be the last major event the company hosts before the holidays. That means it’s going to want to get a lot of bang for its buck this time out.</p>\n<p>The iPhone 12 is expected to be the centerpiece, of course. The headline feature will almost certainly be 5G. Apple’s been a little behind the curve on that front versus its Android competitors (Samsung, for instance, has several devices with next-gen wireless), though another knock-on effect from the pandemic has been a slower than expected adoption of the tech. So in some ways, Apple’s really right on time here. In the U.S., the company is said to offer both the mmWave and sub-6Ghz 5G technologies. Availability may vary depending on the needs of a given market.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"KGrgfTXi93\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/apple-september-15-event-roundup/\">Here&#8217;s everything Apple revealed at its September hardware event</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Here&#8217;s everything Apple revealed at its September hardware event&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/apple-september-15-event-roundup/embed/#?secret=KGrgfTXi93\" data-secret=\"KGrgfTXi93\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Rumors point to a bunch of different models. After all, gone are the days a company like Apple could just offer up a big premium device and be done with it. Sales for high-end devices were already drying up well before the virus came along to bring smartphone sales to a screeching halt there for a bit. People were already tired of paying in excess of $1,000 for new phones when the ones they already had still did the job perfectly fine.</p>\n<p>There are supposedly four sizes arriving. There will be higher-end devices at 6.1 and 6.7 inches, and more budget-minded devices at 6.1 and 5.4 inches. It’s a pretty broad price range, from $699 for the “mini” to $1,099 and up for the Pro Max (sandwiched between are the $799 iPhone 12 and $999 Pro). Along with its recently expanded Watch line, Apple’s all about choice this time out.</p>\n<p>Reportedly, however, the company will be bringing OLED tech to all of the models, marking a pretty big change from the days of LCD-sporting budget models. The new models are expected to get a welcome redesign, reportedly returning to something more in line with the iPhone 5. The rounded edges are expected to be dropped in favor of a flatter design, akin to what you get on the iPad Pro.</p>\n<p>Other interesting potential additions include the return of the company’s dearly departed MagSafe life for a pair of wireless charging pads that will hopefully finally lay to rest any memory of the failed AirPower experiment. Available for one or two devices, the new pads will reportedly leverage magnets built into the phones to snap them in place.</p>\n<p>Music has always been a cornerstone for the company, and it’s long overdue for some updates to audio products. This time out, we may finally get the long-awaited AirPods Studio, an over-ear addition to its line of headphones. The models are set to come in two variations, the largest variation being build materials. A smaller version of its smart speaker could be on the way, as well. The HomePod has long been cost-prohibitive for many, so a mini version could finally make it a bit more accessible.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"PyGPLqmvqr\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/17/a-closer-look-at-the-new-apple-watches/\">A closer look at the new Apple Watches</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;A closer look at the new Apple Watches&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/17/a-closer-look-at-the-new-apple-watches/embed/#?secret=PyGPLqmvqr\" data-secret=\"PyGPLqmvqr\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Another long-rumored addition — AirTags — could finally arrive, as well. Apple’s product-tracking Tile competitor has been in the cards for some time now, but has repeatedly been delayed. That may still be the case — and same goes for a refresh to Apple TV. With the company’s subscription service about to celebrate its year anniversary, it could really use some updated hardware. New Macs with Apple-built chips could be on the table, as well, though the company is reportedly planning one more 2020 event for that big launch.</p>\n<p>The event kicks off tomorrow at <strong>10AM PT/1PM ET.</strong> We’ll be watching along with you, bringing you the news as it breaks.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/apple-iphone-event-2020\"><img id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Like many folks this year, I have been cooking a lot. Though I’ve always loved food and have had a deep and abiding interest for the art of cooking, I’ve definitely pushed myself to learn how to do a lot of things from scratch in the kitchen this year. From cooking a <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CASE2jGpHZH/?igshid=187hbhj9c308b\">decent CTM</a> to a <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CEe5XuYJBol/?igshid=bhzgay6x90uv\">respectable pie</a>, I have hit a lot of my personal milestones over the past few months.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One of the unforeseen consequences of my culinarily driven efforts to stay sane during quarantine this year has been a foray into testing out purpose driven kitchen devices. Though not quite single use (and actually pretty versatile in their own way) </span><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/14/oonis-koda-16-pizza-oven-is-the-rare-kitchen-gadget-that-delivers-on-its-promise/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">devices like the Ooni pizza oven</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and the Otto Grill have found their way into my ad-hoc outdoor kitchen and I have had a pretty enjoyable time pushing and prodding on them while simultaneously upping my own cooking game.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Which leads me to this review of the </span><a href=\"https://www.ottogrills.com/ottos-grills/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Otto Wilde Grill</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><b>What is it?</b></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-large wp-image-2059088\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_5885-1.jpeg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"510\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_5885-1.jpeg 4032w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_5885-1.jpeg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_5885-1.jpeg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_5885-1.jpeg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_5885-1.jpeg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_5885-1.jpeg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_5885-1.jpeg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_5885-1.jpeg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s a 16x17x11” self-contained propane broiler that features two top mounted burners that can reach temperatures of 1,500 degrees F. There is an adjustable grille and a catch pan for grease and a dual use arm that acts as a grille tool and a wrench to adjust the distance between the burners and your food.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s designed to cook steak that gets you as close to steakhouse taste and texture as possible. It does so by mimicking the kinds of top mounted broilers that you’ll find in many commercial kitchens.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I’m not going to bury the lede, this thing is $1,000. If you don’t have a G to drop on a cooking thing of any sort, then read on for entertainment and edification. If you DO have that much to spend (maybe) and are wondering why the hell you’d want to,</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> I think I can deliver those things for you here.</span></p>\n<p><b>But, why</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">After my </span><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/14/oonis-koda-16-pizza-oven-is-the-rare-kitchen-gadget-that-delivers-on-its-promise/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Ooni review</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Otto Wilde Grills reached out to see if I wanted to try out their over-fired broiler. I love steak, especially steak at the perfect temp with a restaurant-style carmelized crust. I’ve been able to get decent results over the years with my standard grill and a cast iron skillet &#8212; and more recently have been very happy with the sous vide bath + skillet method.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But there is just something about the somewhat violent, crispy, high heat broiler style finish that you get at a steakhouse that I have not been able to duplicate at home. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Very specifically, the reason that a steakhouse steak hits your table with a carmel crust and nicely distributed interior juice is something called the </span><a href=\"https://modernistcuisine.com/mc/the-maillard-reaction/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Maillard reaction</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Maillard reactions are different than caramelization, which is basically the heat driven decomposition of sugar. Instead, it is the breakdown and combination of sugars and amino acids. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It happens during cooking in many foods but is most important in great tasting meat and bread. It begins to occur in most foods above around 280 </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">°</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">F or so but even higher temperatures can emphasize the resulting effects to the point where you get this deliciously beautiful light brown crust that adds a crunch and even slight sweetness to your foods, especially meats. </span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059080 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ADE20672-2A87-41FD-81B2-B3D48D606B29_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ADE20672-2A87-41FD-81B2-B3D48D606B29_1_105_c.jpeg 1024w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ADE20672-2A87-41FD-81B2-B3D48D606B29_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ADE20672-2A87-41FD-81B2-B3D48D606B29_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ADE20672-2A87-41FD-81B2-B3D48D606B29_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ADE20672-2A87-41FD-81B2-B3D48D606B29_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/ADE20672-2A87-41FD-81B2-B3D48D606B29_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059093 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/F82F10EB-753D-4D88-8354-2726F9685ECC_1_106_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"872\" height=\"654\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/F82F10EB-753D-4D88-8354-2726F9685ECC_1_106_c.jpeg 872w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/F82F10EB-753D-4D88-8354-2726F9685ECC_1_106_c.jpeg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/F82F10EB-753D-4D88-8354-2726F9685ECC_1_106_c.jpeg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/F82F10EB-753D-4D88-8354-2726F9685ECC_1_106_c.jpeg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/F82F10EB-753D-4D88-8354-2726F9685ECC_1_106_c.jpeg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/F82F10EB-753D-4D88-8354-2726F9685ECC_1_106_c.jpeg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 872px) 100vw, 872px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The trick of at home Maillard reactions in steak is how to activate and sustain the process long enough to create the desired result while simultaneously not over-cooking your meat. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A note: I am reviewing the Otto grill several years after it was initially released (though they do have a new ‘Pro’ model with a really handy drawer and a </span><a href=\"https://product.ottogrills.com/ottos-platform\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">whole grill system</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> hitting the market). But when they offered to send me one I went and checked out the reviews that were out there. Gonna be honest, even the ‘good’ reviews are pretty poorly done. Either they are done on YouTube by clear grillmasters that assume people know a lot about grilling and don’t really explain much beyond running a steak or two through the grill or they are on&#8230;ahem&#8230;other sites where they quite clearly have no idea what they are doing. Don’t get me started on the results in some of those reviews. I can’t even. I’m not going to blow up anyone’s spot specifically here, but as a bit of meta I can just say that the current state of food appliance reviews is really, really bad. I think a lot of people do pretty decent jobs reviewing, say, phones or game consoles. Not so much in the kitchen.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059081 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/5DDF9B9C-7996-4A64-BB77-8968B8FFA27D_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"768\" height=\"1024\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/5DDF9B9C-7996-4A64-BB77-8968B8FFA27D_1_105_c.jpeg 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/5DDF9B9C-7996-4A64-BB77-8968B8FFA27D_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=113,150 113w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/5DDF9B9C-7996-4A64-BB77-8968B8FFA27D_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=225,300 225w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/5DDF9B9C-7996-4A64-BB77-8968B8FFA27D_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=510,680 510w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/5DDF9B9C-7996-4A64-BB77-8968B8FFA27D_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Anyway, over-fired broilers are </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">extremely</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> common in commercial kitchens, where ‘infrared’ heat (basically high heat gas shot through pinholes in a ceramic sheet) and radiant heat are primary options. The Otto Grill is an infrared style OFB, which means that it can get to high heat extremely quickly (about 3-5 minutes to 1,500 degrees) and that it cooks VERY fast because most of the heat goes right to the meat. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Fast, high heat cooking means quicker crust, less gas waste and most importantly, juicier steaks that have less time to dry out. </span></p>\n<p><b>A quick how-to</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One of the things that I found surprising when I started researching the Otto was that there are very few direct examples of how to cook a steak with it. To that end, here is my basic process for most steaks. Prior to beginning any of this I salt my steaks generously with a nice sea salt. I do not use anything else personally and I would say beware of any rubs with pepper or other ingredients because they can burn quickly in an oven as hot as the Otto.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone size-full wp-image-2059097\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/DAC645E9-1135-4C76-9C89-2968619A4FD0_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/DAC645E9-1135-4C76-9C89-2968619A4FD0_1_105_c.jpeg 1024w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/DAC645E9-1135-4C76-9C89-2968619A4FD0_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/DAC645E9-1135-4C76-9C89-2968619A4FD0_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/DAC645E9-1135-4C76-9C89-2968619A4FD0_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/DAC645E9-1135-4C76-9C89-2968619A4FD0_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/DAC645E9-1135-4C76-9C89-2968619A4FD0_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<ol>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Fill the water tray halfway. This prevents grease fires and makes cleanup better, as well as introducing a bit of moisture to the cooking environment. </span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Pre-heat the Otto at full power. This takes as little as 3 minutes and no longer than 5 from zero to 1,500 degrees. </span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Remove the grille and place the steak(s) onto it oriented so that they are covered by one or both burners. </span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Pop it back in and use the adjustment lever to move them within about a half inch of the bottom edge of the flame at the top. You should see a roiling, sizzling field of flame turbulence just above the top surface of the meat. </span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Cook for around 60 seconds to 90 seconds. </span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Lower, remove, and flip end over end to sear the other side. </span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Raise, and cook for another 60-90 seconds. </span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">At this point, if your steak is 1” thick or under and you are ok with medium rare, you are likely done. Remove it and check the temp with a meat thermometer to see if it is at your desired temp.</span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If it is a thicker cut, reduce the heat to ¾ on both burners and drop the grill to the bottom position. Rotate every 2 minutes and periodically check the meat temp (I do it out of the oven because it’s so hot in there) until you hit desired done levels.</span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Remove the meat to rest, turn off the Otto and let cool somewhat to clean the tray and grille.</span></li>\n</ol>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This method has enabled me to cook thinner cuts in as little as 3-5 minutes. Larger cuts may require careful rotation and positioning. </span></p>\n<p><b>Steak results</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I have cooked a lot of steaks on the Otto over the last couple of months. I’ve done ribeye, sirloin, filet mignon, hangar and T-bone</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I cooked a wide variety of cuts at a number of different levels of marbling. The fattier cuts obviously benefited much more from the Otto’s high-temp cooking. The way that it absolutely pulverizes fat allows it to crust perfectly across the surface without creating a dry, crumbly texture. Instead it’s crispy and moist at the same time. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Also, because it’s a top firing burner, the fat seeps downward, through the meat instead of outwards. The resulting exterior is super delicious and produces a nearly perfectly sized rind every time, leaving a to-temp interior. </span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059079 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/B28426E9-9FD7-4B15-A623-6B7EBFC394AD_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/B28426E9-9FD7-4B15-A623-6B7EBFC394AD_1_105_c.jpeg 1024w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/B28426E9-9FD7-4B15-A623-6B7EBFC394AD_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/B28426E9-9FD7-4B15-A623-6B7EBFC394AD_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/B28426E9-9FD7-4B15-A623-6B7EBFC394AD_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/B28426E9-9FD7-4B15-A623-6B7EBFC394AD_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/B28426E9-9FD7-4B15-A623-6B7EBFC394AD_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It took me a few steaks to get the methodology above down. I burned a few, for sure. This thing is crazy hot and the times involved are hard to wrap your head around at first. But once you have your rhythm, the Otto Grill cooks an insanely tasty steak from nearly any cut or quality of meat. Otto sent me a few frozen steaks to try, but I’ve mostly cooked my own meat purchased locally, which was much better. But even thawed meat was treated pretty well by this grill, the crust makes up for a lot when you’re working with so-so meat. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">For those of you that know steak, you may be wondering whether it is good at grassfed beef. Yes! It’s actually super killer for grassfed because the high, high heat makes the sear happen super fast, locking in the juice which is at a big premium in leaner grassfed cuts. Grassfed suffers with long cook times, which you won’t find in the Otto. You can cook a very nicely juicy medium rare grassfed cut here.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One major comparison that I think many people who might be in the market to buy this thing will be interested in is how it stacks up against the very popular sous-vide + cast iron sear method also referred to as reverse searing. Cooking your steak in a water bath to achieve precise interior temp and then searing it for crust and flavor has become uber popular for at home cooks in recent years due to the wide availability of consumer grade immersion circulators. </span></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059075\" style=\"width: 778px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2059075\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2059075 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/79274190-C8EE-4F06-B94B-1321AD9D53AF_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"768\" height=\"1024\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/79274190-C8EE-4F06-B94B-1321AD9D53AF_1_105_c.jpeg 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/79274190-C8EE-4F06-B94B-1321AD9D53AF_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=113,150 113w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/79274190-C8EE-4F06-B94B-1321AD9D53AF_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=225,300 225w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/79274190-C8EE-4F06-B94B-1321AD9D53AF_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=510,680 510w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/79274190-C8EE-4F06-B94B-1321AD9D53AF_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2059075\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Sous-vide + sear on left, Otto Grill on right</p></div></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I’ll say this as simply as possible: I think you can get </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">extremely similar</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> results with sous vide + cast iron, with some pretty straightforward caveats. </span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Your cast iron has to be super hot. I’m talking 2,000 BTUs and up of gas burner hot. You need that high, hot heat to get that sear to retain moisture and render your fat quickly. </span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You’re searing it from the </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">bottom by contact</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> rather than the </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">top by proximity</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, which means that fat will have a tendency to boil away and you need to continuously circulate your juices using butter or another oil. </span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Smoke and spatter. You’re going to generate plenty of both on a skillet. </span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059076\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2059076\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2059076 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/E77BFB3D-A150-482D-981E-6E5118F9D98A_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/E77BFB3D-A150-482D-981E-6E5118F9D98A_1_105_c.jpeg 1024w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/E77BFB3D-A150-482D-981E-6E5118F9D98A_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/E77BFB3D-A150-482D-981E-6E5118F9D98A_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/E77BFB3D-A150-482D-981E-6E5118F9D98A_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/E77BFB3D-A150-482D-981E-6E5118F9D98A_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/E77BFB3D-A150-482D-981E-6E5118F9D98A_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2059076\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Sous-vide + sear on left, Otto Grill on right</p></div></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you’re really used to reverse searing and you love your results, I still do think there are a couple of areas where the Otto can up your game a bit, but the general taste and satisfaction will be in the ballpark. One thing I did try which worked out well is a tri-tip &#8212; a huge cut that is popular in California that would not do well normally here. I did a sous-vide bath + reverse sear <em>in the Otto</em> and those turned out really lovely. </span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-2059084 size-large\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/03D4F7F1-1607-4842-B53B-2654590D914C_1_102_o.jpeg?w=510\" alt=\"\" width=\"510\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/03D4F7F1-1607-4842-B53B-2654590D914C_1_102_o.jpeg 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/03D4F7F1-1607-4842-B53B-2654590D914C_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=113,150 113w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/03D4F7F1-1607-4842-B53B-2654590D914C_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=225,300 225w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/03D4F7F1-1607-4842-B53B-2654590D914C_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=768,1024 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/03D4F7F1-1607-4842-B53B-2654590D914C_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=510,680 510w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/03D4F7F1-1607-4842-B53B-2654590D914C_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=1152,1536 1152w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/03D4F7F1-1607-4842-B53B-2654590D914C_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 510px) 100vw, 510px\" /> <img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059085 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/7DEF1BAA-EA37-49C1-AAA9-68EF1DEEBF35_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"768\" height=\"1024\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/7DEF1BAA-EA37-49C1-AAA9-68EF1DEEBF35_1_105_c.jpeg 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/7DEF1BAA-EA37-49C1-AAA9-68EF1DEEBF35_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=113,150 113w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/7DEF1BAA-EA37-49C1-AAA9-68EF1DEEBF35_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=225,300 225w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/7DEF1BAA-EA37-49C1-AAA9-68EF1DEEBF35_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=510,680 510w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/7DEF1BAA-EA37-49C1-AAA9-68EF1DEEBF35_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059083 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C724D69-8D98-4853-A9D8-4D81AFAB5205_1_102_o.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1536\" height=\"2048\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C724D69-8D98-4853-A9D8-4D81AFAB5205_1_102_o.jpeg 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C724D69-8D98-4853-A9D8-4D81AFAB5205_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=113,150 113w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C724D69-8D98-4853-A9D8-4D81AFAB5205_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=225,300 225w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C724D69-8D98-4853-A9D8-4D81AFAB5205_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=768,1024 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C724D69-8D98-4853-A9D8-4D81AFAB5205_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=510,680 510w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C724D69-8D98-4853-A9D8-4D81AFAB5205_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=1152,1536 1152w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C724D69-8D98-4853-A9D8-4D81AFAB5205_1_102_o.jpeg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1536px) 100vw, 1536px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I liked the Otto’s more delineated rind that creates that nice flavor seal along the interior edge of your cut of meat. I also think that it can be very easy to over cook thin steaks while searing if you can’t get your skillet super hot. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The biggest overall benefit of course, is time. If you write off the resting time to bring your meat to room temp, which is passive cooking time, then you’re looking at anywhere from 1-3 hours to sous vide a thick cut steak. The Otto heats in 3 minutes and cooks in anywhere from 5-10 minutes. It’s a huge time savings for equal or better results.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One design consideration worth mentioning is that because there are two burners with a dead space in between, you must shift larger cuts to allow them to sear evenly if they span two burners. I wouldn’t call it a flaw as it is definitely pushing it to shove a wall-to-wall steak in there. I would love to see future versions of the oven reduce the space between the burners in order to allow more coverage for bigger steaks. This is a non factor if your steak fits under one burner, and most do in general. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The catch pan, by the way, is pretty instrumental. Filling it with water reduces the chances that your fat will catch on fire, burning portions of your steak, and it makes cleaning up super easy as you can sluice out the still warm grease water and then brush it clean. I will note, at the risk of some ribbing, that I forgot to put some water in the pan once and may have added some&#8230;decorative smoke work to my grill’s face. Cook outdoors.</span></p>\n<p><b>Pizza</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Otto says you can make pizza in this thing too &#8212; and they even make a stone and peel. Well, you can, but I&#8217;d say how enthusiastic you get about it is going to sort of depend on what your standards for pizza are. </span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059066 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/C5048398-8BED-4C77-97DA-F5CD6922D7EF_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"768\" height=\"1024\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/C5048398-8BED-4C77-97DA-F5CD6922D7EF_1_105_c.jpeg 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/C5048398-8BED-4C77-97DA-F5CD6922D7EF_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=113,150 113w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/C5048398-8BED-4C77-97DA-F5CD6922D7EF_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=225,300 225w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/C5048398-8BED-4C77-97DA-F5CD6922D7EF_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=510,680 510w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/C5048398-8BED-4C77-97DA-F5CD6922D7EF_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059065 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/2107C5B0-4408-4289-87D0-3A30AAB58C90_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"768\" height=\"1024\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/2107C5B0-4408-4289-87D0-3A30AAB58C90_1_105_c.jpeg 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/2107C5B0-4408-4289-87D0-3A30AAB58C90_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=113,150 113w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/2107C5B0-4408-4289-87D0-3A30AAB58C90_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=225,300 225w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/2107C5B0-4408-4289-87D0-3A30AAB58C90_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=510,680 510w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/2107C5B0-4408-4289-87D0-3A30AAB58C90_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The pizzas that I made in the Otto with the stone are, uh, they’re fine I guess. It’s absolutely, totally possible to do a little personal-sized pizza in the Otto, especially if you par bake the crust. But anything you do in here is going to pale next to the Ooni. I’d actually much rather just gin a up a little pan pizza that you can do in your regular home oven. There are a lot of reasons to buy the Otto, but pizza should not be a primary one, in my opinion.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout aligncenter wp-image-2059067 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C7BE49A-6984-4C89-847F-7E2A82D95495_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"768\" height=\"1024\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C7BE49A-6984-4C89-847F-7E2A82D95495_1_105_c.jpeg 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C7BE49A-6984-4C89-847F-7E2A82D95495_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=113,150 113w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C7BE49A-6984-4C89-847F-7E2A82D95495_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=225,300 225w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C7BE49A-6984-4C89-847F-7E2A82D95495_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=510,680 510w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/0C7BE49A-6984-4C89-847F-7E2A82D95495_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /> <img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059068 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/084CBF2C-1A41-417A-B7A7-FD1F56A184D5_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"768\" height=\"1024\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/084CBF2C-1A41-417A-B7A7-FD1F56A184D5_1_105_c.jpeg 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/084CBF2C-1A41-417A-B7A7-FD1F56A184D5_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=113,150 113w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/084CBF2C-1A41-417A-B7A7-FD1F56A184D5_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=225,300 225w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/084CBF2C-1A41-417A-B7A7-FD1F56A184D5_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=510,680 510w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/084CBF2C-1A41-417A-B7A7-FD1F56A184D5_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></p>\n<p>I did cook a beautiful batch of naan in it though which was lovely. It&#8217;s basically common sense. Anything in the flatbread family is going to do wonderful here, but stuff with toppings needs to be par baked because it&#8217;s so damn hot.</p>\n<p><b>Other stuff</b></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2059077 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/FA4D9713-5713-43DD-B0BC-7DD1A7E3AE65_1_105_c.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/FA4D9713-5713-43DD-B0BC-7DD1A7E3AE65_1_105_c.jpeg 1024w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/FA4D9713-5713-43DD-B0BC-7DD1A7E3AE65_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/FA4D9713-5713-43DD-B0BC-7DD1A7E3AE65_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/FA4D9713-5713-43DD-B0BC-7DD1A7E3AE65_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/FA4D9713-5713-43DD-B0BC-7DD1A7E3AE65_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/FA4D9713-5713-43DD-B0BC-7DD1A7E3AE65_1_105_c.jpeg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Can you cook other stuff in the Otto? Yeah, 100%. Basically anything you can throw in a cast iron pan and sear up will do well in the Otto. Examples I’ve tried include peppers and onions, fruit and veg medleys and crispy potatoes drizzled in oil. Because the cast iron gets nice and evenly hot and you have a top broiler it makes for an ideal searing environment. It is hot as hell even at the lower settings though, so you need to keep an eye on it. </span></p>\n<p><b>Should you buy it?</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Otto Wilde likely have their own ideas about the target market for their grills but for me it&#8217;s: has disposable income, loves steak enough to eat it 3x a week and already owns at least one or two other specialty grilling items. Basically, Big Green Egg owners. While something like a BGE is amazing at low and slow and smoking, it takes a hell of a lot to stoke and maintain the heat you’d need to get a caramelizing sear and in the end your steak would definitely be dryer. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Otto Grill is basically the consumerized version of a commercial kitchen staple item. Could you buy </span><a href=\"https://www.katom.com/083-TASM24NG.html?gclid=Cj0KCQjw2or8BRCNARIsAC_ppyYnt5zlIyDFcnypw9n9n29GWkxikp5LWegRqC5r8SESlWS6ZD7_NooaAnaJEALw_wcB\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">something like a Salamander</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> for like $1,300? Sure, but at that point you’re a commercial kitchen and you’re gonna need a natural gas plumb and probably a business license. Just rent a strip mall slot or a food truck. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Overall I found the design to be thoughtful, straightforward and reliable. Though I did have some ignition issues as described earlier, this is frank German engineering at its most utility-driven. The Otto Grill is expensive, but does precisely perform the task that it claims to make possible. I have cooked steaks by many different methods over the years and as I mentioned above, some of them are absolute stand-bys because they are really close to restaurant methodology. But for </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">steakhouse</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> style crust delivered absolutely consistently with the minimum of </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">time and effort</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, the Otto Grill stands alone.</span></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a
